State v. Calhoun


No. 104, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


306 Md. 692; 511 A.2d 461; 1986 Md. LEXIS 265



July 15, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied August 21, 1986.
Writ of certiorari denied Calhoun v. Maryland, 480 U.S. 910, 107 S. Ct. 1339, 94 L. Ed. 2d 528, 1987 U.S. LEXIS 939 (Mar. 2, 1987)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court for Montgomery County, James S. McAuliffe, Judge.
Calhoun v. State, 297 Md. 563, 468 A.2d 45, 1983 Md. LEXIS 322 (Nov. 21, 1983)
Tichnell v. Maryland, 467 U.S. 1268, 104 S. Ct. 3564, 82 L. Ed. 2d 865, 1984 U.S. LEXIS 332, 52 U.S.L.W. 3920 (June 25, 1984)



DISPOSITION: ORDER OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY GRANTING A NEW CAPITAL SENTENCING PROCEEDING REVERSED; IN ALL OTHER RESPECTS, THE ORDER OF THAT COURT IS AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR THE PURPOSE OF ENTERING AN ORDER DENYING ALL POST-CONVICTION RELIEF TO JAMES ARTHUR CALHOUN.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief challenging his convictions for two murders and the death sentence imposed against him. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) affirmed his convictions but ordered a new sentencing proceeding, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of premeditated murder, felony murder, and lesser charges. In a capital sentencing proceeding, the jury determined that the aggravating factors outweighed the mitigating factors, and defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant claimed that the trial court's failure to give him an opportunity to speak to the jury on his own behalf concerning mitigating factors violated his rights. He also claimed that his attorney's failure to inform him that he had a right to allocution deprived him of the effective assistance of counsel. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a new capital sentencing proceeding on either ground. In so holding, the court ruled that (1) defendant was sentenced at a time when there was no rule of criminal procedure in effect governing the right to allocution; (2) the right to allocution was not a fundamental right; (3) defendant waived his right to allocution by failing to request an opportunity to address the jury prior to sentencing; and (4) the attorney's failure to inform defendant of his right to allocution did not constitute ineffective assistance because the law on the right to allocution was unclear at that time.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order granting a new capital sentencing proceeding, but otherwise affirmed the order of the lower court and remanded the case with instructions to enter an order denying all post-conviction relief to defendant.

 

239 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Broadwater v. State


No. 132, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


306 Md. 597; 510 A.2d 583; 1986 Md. LEXIS 305



July 1, 1986 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted felon on probation (felon), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted summary judgment for appellee state in the felon's action to have Md. Const. art. I, § 12 declared unconstitutional because it violated the Equal Protection Clause or, alternatively, that § 12 should not be applied to him if he elected to run as a state senator two years later.


OVERVIEW: The felon had been a former state senator and had been convicted of conspiracy, unauthorized acquisition of food stamps, and aiding and abetting in federal court. He had served his prison time and was on probation when his action was commenced. Md. Const. art. I, § 12 provided that one running for an elective state office had to be a registered voter. Under Md. Ann. Code art. 33, § 3-4(c), the felon could not become a registered voter until he served his probationary period. The court affirmed the judgment that Md. Const. art. I, § 12 was constitutional. The felon had standing to represent the class of all unregistered voters who were barred from elective office. The court found under the Equal Protection Clause, strict scrutiny was not required because of the ease of registration of unregistered voters to meet the registration requirements. The court found that the constitutional amendment made uniform a requirement that those holding elective office be registered voters. Thus, the felon was not entitled to become a candidate for any constitutionally created office unless he complied with the requirements imposed by the laws in the year of the election.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the state in the felon's action to declare unconstitutional an amendment to the state constitution that a person had to be a registered voter to hold elective office.

Knill v. Knill


No. 39, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


306 Md. 527; 510 A.2d 546; 1986 Md. LEXIS 245



June 27, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Frederick County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Samuel W. Barrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY REVERSED. APPELLEE TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Frederick County (Maryland), which found that the husband was equitably estopped from denying an obligation to support a child born to appellee wife during wedlock.


OVERVIEW: A husband challenged an order prohibiting him from denying his obligation to pay child support. The issue before the court was whether a husband could be required to support a child who, though born to his wife during wedlock, was not sired by him. On appeal, the court reversed the order and held that the husband was not equitably estopped to deny a duty to support the child. The court found that it was reasonable to infer that the husband intended that the child should have considered the husband to be his father. The court also found that the child used the husband's surname. Yet, the court determined that the evidence failed to support even an inference that the husband's voluntary support caused the wife to forego the possibility of pursuing support from the child's natural father. The court also determined that the child incurred no financial loss as a result of his relationship with the husband.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order equitably estopping the husband from disclaiming his duty to pay child support.

Chevy Chase Sav. & Loan, Inc. v. State


No. 9, September Term, 1986


Court of Appeals of Maryland


306 Md. 384; 509 A.2d 670; 1986 Md. LEXIS 240



June 5, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Joseph H. H. Kaplan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY CHEVY CHASE SAVINGS AND LOAN, INC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state chartered association filed a breach of contract action to recover funds that it had been assessed for the insurance of its deposit accounts through an insolvent state insurer. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) entered judgment for defendant state and state deposit agency, the insolvent state insurer's successor by merger. The state chartered association filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: A state chartered association contributed a portion of its free share accounts to a state insurer as required by state law. The state insurer became insolvent and merged with the state deposit agency. After the merger, the state chartered association withdrew its membership and demanded the return of its insurance fund and central reserve fund contributions. The request was denied and the state chartered association filed a breach of contract action. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment because the state and the state deposit agency had not breached contracts relating to the repayment of the contributions. The court found that (1) the insolvent state insurer's bylaws were extinguished by the merger, (2) the state chartered association was not entitled to a return of its insurance fund contributions unless money remained in the fund after net insurable losses of each free share account were paid, (3) the state chartered association was entitled to a return of its central reserve fund contributions when the liquidity problems of member associations were resolved, and (4) no unconstitutional taking of assets had occurred by the delay in repayment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which held that the state and state deposit agency had not breach a contract with a state-chartered association relating to the repayment of insurance fund and central reserve fund contributions.

Booth v. State


No. 151, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


306 Md. 172; 507 A.2d 1098; 1986 Md. LEXIS 231



May 7, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City, Edward J. Angeletti, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) convicted defendant of two counts of murder in the first degree, robbery, and conspiracy to rob. Defendant was sentenced to death and appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant murdered an elderly couple in the victims' home and stole jewelry. Each victim was stabbed in the chest, after having been bound and gagged. That same night defendant and co-defendant borrowed a car and drove with their girlfriends back to the victims' home to collect more property. The girlfriends saw the murdered bodies. Defendant did not testify at trial. However, during the sentencing phase, he gave an allocution under Md. R. Crim. Causes 4-343 in which he denied killing anyone, but admitted entering the victims' home to steal. In summation, the State told the jury that defendant's statement was not evidence, that defendant chose not to testify to avoid cross-examination, and that defendant had lied to the jury. The court held that defendant's allocution was testimonial and that he had waived any right under the U.S. Const. amend. V to avoid comment by the prosecutor on the allocution. The court further held that a victim impact statement was properly submitted to the jury. The court also held that there was sufficient evidence to support the conspiracy conviction because there was evidence that defendant and co-defendant had acted in concert.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentence.

Bowers v. State


No. 122, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


306 Md. 120; 507 A.2d 1072; 1986 Md. LEXIS 232



May 7, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Charles County, George W. Bowling, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree. A jury in the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland) sentenced defendant to death. The court affirmed the conviction, but vacated the death sentence and remanded the case for a new sentencing proceeding. A jury again sentenced defendant to death. Pursuant to the provisions of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 414 (1957), the court reviewed defendant's sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he strangled the victim, but raised several issues on appeal. The court held that: (1) defendant, who was in the position of a convicted felon awaiting sentence, was not clothed with a presumption of innocence; (2) the trial judge properly exercised his discretion in determining that defendant had to wear leg irons while in the court room due to the serious nature of the charges and defendant's prior behavior; (3) the autopsy report was properly admitted as evidence pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. I § 5-311(d)(1),(2) (1982); (4) defendant failed to make a specific request to include possible other mitigating circumstances on the written verdict form submitted to the jury; (5) the evidence supported the jury's finding that the statutory aggravating circumstances were not outweighed by the mitigating circumstances; and (6) the sentence was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases, nor was it imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. Thus, the court held that the death sentence was appropriate under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of death.

Finding that none of the grounds for reversal warranted such action, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of guilt and imposition of the death penalty.

245 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Huebner


No. 94, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


305 Md. 601; 505 A.2d 1331; 1986 Md. LEXIS 208



March 24, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with crimes within the district court's jurisdiction. They demanded a jury trial and the state announced that it would seek sentences less than 89 days. At the start of trial, the state entered a nolle prosequi to all but one charge. Defendants sought a determination in the circuit court of their right to a jury trial. The petition was denied, the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed, and certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the district court lost jurisdiction after they sought a jury trial and that the state's nolle prosequi of all charges on which a jury could be demanded were ineffective. The state claimed that the district court retained jurisdiction and its nolle prosequi were effective. The court agreed with defendants and affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court held that the right to a jury trial attached to the crime of resisting arrest and that the state acted improperly in entering nolle prosequi to all the charges except disorderly conduct. The court also held that, under the plain language of Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 4-302, the district court was deprived of jurisdiction when defendants demanded a jury trial and that the only remaining function for the district court was to determine defendants' entitlement to a jury trial. The court also held that in all other respects, the district court's jurisdiction was lost and the jurisdiction of the circuit court attached. The court further held that once the circuit court obtained jurisdiction, it could not thereafter be divested. Thus, the court held that the entry of the nolle prosequi was a nullity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

State v. Smith


No. 126, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


305 Md. 489; 505 A.2d 511; 1986 Md. LEXIS 204



March 6, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Robert J. Gerstung, Judge.



DISPOSITION: MOTION TO DISMISS APPEAL DENIED; MOTION TO DISMISS WRIT OF CERTIORARI DENIED; JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS; COSTS TO BE PAID BY JANET SMITH.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) which dismissed a statement of charges against defendant for theft of a bicycle.


OVERVIEW: A civilian applied to the district court for a statement of charges alleging the theft of a bicycle. A judicial officer, referred to as a commissioner, issued the statement. Defendant's motion to dismiss the statement was granted, and state sought review. The court reversed and remanded that matter because a commissioner had never been required to issue a statement of charges when a defendant is arrested without a warrant. The power of a commissioner to issue a warrant of arrest was bestowed by constitution, statute and rule. "Warrants of arrest" as used in Md. Const. art. IV, § 41G was a generic term which included a statement of charges within the meaning of the Maryland Rules. The issuance of statements of charges by commissioners was not prohibited by the principle of separation of powers, and the commissioners were sufficiently neutral and detached.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the statement of charges and remanded the case.

 

247 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. State


No. 89, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


305 Md. 357; 504 A.2d 626; 1986 Md. LEXIS 197



February 24, 1986, Opinion


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Order January 10, 1985. Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Wicomico County - Judge Richard M. Pollitt)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which concluded that defendant's demand for a jury trial did not deprive a district court of jurisdiction upon defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari. Defendant had been convicted by the district court of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a writ of certiorari contending that she should have been granted a jury trial. The court found that defendant had made a timely demand for a trial by jury. The State then recommended, and the district court agreed, that defendant would receive a sentence of not longer than 90 days should she be found guilty. Thus, the district court pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 4-302(d)(2)(ii) (1984), denied defendant's demand for a jury trial. Defendant argued that her timely demand for a trial by jury deprived the district court of jurisdiction and that the application of § 4-302(d)(2)(ii) unconstitutionally deprived her of a jury trial. The court stated that § 4-302(d)(2)(ii) was invalid as applied to one charged with driving while intoxicated under Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 21-902(a). Therefore, defendant was entitled to a jury trial and the district court erred in denying defendant's timely request for the jury trial. Because the district court was deprived of jurisdiction, the case was ordered to be remanded for a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and the cause was remanded for a jury trial.

O'Hara v. Kovens


No. 30, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


305 Md. 280; 503 A.2d 1313; 1986 Md. LEXIS 185



February 3, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City - Judge Elsbeth Levy Bothe).



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS FOR THE RESPONDENTS, IRVIN KOVENS ET AL., AND AGAINST THE PETITIONERS, MICHAEL O'HARA AND JAMES FRANCIS O'HARA, INDIVIDUALLY, REVERSED. JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS FOR THE CROSS-RESPONDENTS, MICHAEL O'HARA AND JAMES FRANCIS O'HARA, AS PERSONAL REPRESENTATIVES OF THE ESTATE OF JOSEPHINE O'HARA, AND AGAINST THE CROSS-PETITIONERS, IRVIN KOVENS ET AL., AFFIRMED. CASES REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AND TO REMAND TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENTS AND CROSS-PETITIONERS, IRVIN KOVENS ET AL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sellers petitioned for certiorari on a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirming in part and reversing in part summary judgment to defendant purchasers against plaintiffs' assertions that defendants conspired to defraud them. The court found that plaintiffs had not met the requirements of the statute of limitations, but reversed summary judgment in one instance because of one plaintiff's mental instability.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sellers asserted that defendant purchasers had conspired to defraud them. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the lower court's decision granting defendants summary judgment against most of plaintiffs' claims on the theory that plaintiffs had not met the requirements of the statute of limitations, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-201. The court affirmed the lower court's decision to reverse summary judgment against one plaintiff whose mental disability rendered applications of the statute of limitations unfair. However, the court reversed the lower court's grant of summary judgment regarding the rest of the action, finding that questions of fact on which a defense based on limitations will turn out to be decided by the jury, or by the court sitting as a jury. The court, therefore, found that the lower court improperly acted as a jury when it reached decisions based on factual questions related to the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the lower court's judgement, affirming its decision to reverse summary judgment regarding the plaintiff seller suffering mental disability. Questions of fact on which a defense based on the statute of limitations will turn should be decided by the jury, or by the court sitting as a jury, and, therefore, the lower court had acted outside of its province in reaching its decision.

 

249 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. State


Nos. 43, 91, 66, 98, 64, 133, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


305 Md. 306; 503 A.2d 1326; 1986 Md. LEXIS 183



February 3, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY: Foster v. State, 304 Md. 439, 499 A.2d 1236, 1985 Md. LEXIS 918 (1985)
Huffington v. State, 304 Md. 559, 500 A.2d 272, 1985 Md. LEXIS 881 (1985)
Evans v. State, 304 Md. 487, 499 A.2d 1261, 1985 Md. LEXIS 882 (Nov. 12, 1985)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought reconsideration of the court's previous rulings in their capital cases, which affirmed the judgment in each case, and upheld the imposition of the death penalty. Defendants argued that Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413(h) placed an unconstitutional burden of persuasion on defendants regarding the weight accorded aggravating and mitigating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendants sought reconsideration of the court's previous ruling affirming their death sentences, arguing that § 413(h) placed an unconstitutional burden of persuasion on defendants, and that the court's earlier ruling reconstructed the statute while denying them the benefit of the reconstruction in violation of their due process rights. Defendants also sought reconsideration of a ruling on jury instructions related to § 413(h); and one defendant requested reconsideration of his sentence because a jury was not permitted to hear that a life sentence meant he would never be eligible for parole. The court denied the motions for reconsideration, holding that: 1) the previous ruling had not reconstructed § 413(h), and previous case law had not held that a defendant had the burden of persuasion regarding the weight accorded mitigating and aggravating circumstances; 2) defendants waived objections to jury instructions because they failed to earlier raise the issues; 3) even if the arguments had not been waived, there was no reversible error; and 4) Maryland law precluded the trial court from instructing the jury about the meaning of a life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motions for reconsideration of their death sentences.

 

250 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Burning Tree Club, Inc. v. Bainum


No. 119, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


305 Md. 53; 501 A.2d 817; 1985 Md. LEXIS 895



December 23, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AFFIRMED AS TO THE DECLARATORY JUDGMENT AND REVERSED AS TO THE INJUNCTIVE RELIEF. COSTS TO BE EVENLY DIVIDED BETWEEN APPELLANT AND APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant country club sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which determined that Md. Code Ann. § 19(e) violated Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 46 because its primary purpose allowed appellant to discriminate on the basis of sex and that it was supported by state funds. Appellee female taxpayers were granted an injunction against the state's allowance of further preferential tax treatment to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant country club was an all-male golf club, which received preferential tax assessments by the state, under Md. Code Ann. § 19(e)(4), in exchange for an agreement to preserve open spaces. Appellee female taxpayers sought a judgment invalidating the statute, in that it violated the Equal Rights Amendment (ERA), Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 46. The lower court held that the statute was violative, where its primary purpose allowed appellant to discriminate on the basis of sex, and enjoined the state from granting further tax benefits. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed, holding that the general assembly, by enacting the law, had permitted a discriminatory practice, and that such violated the ERA. The court indicated that it believed that there was no unequal treatment or burdens between the sexes and that the primary purpose provision was sex-neutral. Yet, the discriminatory effect was unlawful, and further, that the primary purpose provision was not severable from the rest of Ch. 870 of the Acts of 1974 , which was the sex discrimination prohibition. Accordingly, the court reversed the injunction against the state as to granting further tax benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which invalidated a statute providing for preferential tax treatments to appellant country club as a violation of the Equal Rights Amendment because the law was sanctioned by the general assembly, which constituted discriminatory state action on the basis of sex. The court reversed the injunction as to further tax preferences, finding that the primary purpose and sex discrimination prohibition were not severable.

State v. Wyand


No. 48, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 721; 501 A.2d 43; 1985 Md. LEXIS 890



December 13, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Washington County, John P. Corderman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; APPELLEES TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland), which dismissed charges against defendants for violations of various gambling laws. The circuit court held that Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 255(a), (b) (1982, 1984 Cum. Supp.), which provided exemptions from the gaming laws for certain organizations, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted in the district court of keeping a gaming table and selling lottery tickets. Defendant appealed, alleging that the statutory exemption for veterans and fraternal organizations was a violation of equal protection. The circuit court agreed and dismissed the charges. The court reversed. The court held as follows: (1) the Equal Protection Clause required that the statute in question have a rational means to serve a legitimate end because the classifications did not pertain to race, alienage, national origin, fundamental rights, gender, or illegitimacy; (2) as a general proposition of law the promotion of general charitable, civic, educational, and public safety purposes was a proper object of legislation; (3) the general assembly could well have concluded that the types of organizations mentioned in § 255(b) were ones contributing by their presence to the general welfare and well-being of the communities in which they existed; and (4) a rational basis existed for the enactment of § 255(a), (b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court dismissing the charges against defendants and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Consumer Protection Div. Office of Attorney Gen. v. Consumer Pub. Co.


No. 88, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 731; 501 A.2d 48; 1985 Md. LEXIS 897



December 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied January 29, 1986.

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CONSUMER PROTECTION DIVISION FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state consumer protection agency (agency) filed charges against respondent company that alleged that the company's advertisements that offered diet pills for sale contained false and misleading statements in violation of the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, Md. Code Ann., Com. Law § 13 et seq. (1983). A hearing was held and the company sought review with the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland). Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court vacated the agency's order and substituted a new order. The trial court determined that the company's constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV had been violated. The company later filed a motion for revision of the judgment, which the trial court denied. The court granted a petition for a writ of certiorari. OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case back to the trial court with directions to remand the case to the agency for further proceedings.

 

253 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. Fitzgerald


Misc. No. 6, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 689; 501 A.2d 27; 1985 Md. LEXIS 888



December 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certification of questions of law from the United States District Court for the District of Maryland.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED AS HEREIN SET FORTH; COSTS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient brought a medical malpractice action against appellant physician after the physician incorrectly diagnosed the patient with multiple sclerosis instead of a spinal tumor. The United States District Court for the District of Maryland certified three questions to the court all relating to the application of the statute of limitation contained within Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-109 (1984).


OVERVIEW: The patient underwent a continuous course of treatment for a single medical condition. That treatment commenced prior to July 1, 1975, and terminated after that date with the physician's initial misdiagnosis occurring prior to July 1, 1975. The patient argued that the statute of limitation in § 5-109 was not applicable to the action. The physician sought summary judgment on the ground that § 5-109 barred the action because the patient failed to file the action within five years after the injury. The court concluded that: (1) § 5-109 did not apply unless the injury occurred prior to July 1, 1975; (2) whether or not the initial misdiagnosis caused an injury prior to July 1, 1975 was a question of fact; (3) the continuing course of treatment doctrine did not alter the accrual date; (4) the common law rule was abrogated by § 5-109 and the statutory periods had to be calculated in accordance with the literal language of the statute; and (5) the limitation periods provided by § 5-109 were not so unreasonably short as to contravene due process.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the Maryland statute of limitations for medical malpractice actions was valid and had to be calculated in accord with the literal terms of the statute for any injury that occurred after July 1, 1975.

 

254 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. State


Nos. 43, 91, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 439; 499 A.2d 1236; 1985 Md. LEXIS 918



November 12, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of felony murder by a jury in the Circuit Court for Cecil County (Maryland). She elected to be sentenced by the trial court and following a hearing, was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court held that certain evidence was erroneously excluded at trial, and reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial. Defendant was convicted again upon re-trial and again sentenced to death. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial, defendant filed a written motion to allow two separate juries for the trial and sentencing stages. She maintained that a jury was "death qualified," a jury from which had been excluded those persons so opposed to capital punishment that they would not be impartial, was more prone to convict and was neither impartial nor indifferent. She argued on appeal that the denial of her pretrial motion for two separate juries, and the striking for cause of a prospective juror who was so opposed to capital punishment that his impartiality would be affected, unconstitutionally deprived her of an impartial and a representative jury at the guilt or innocence phase of the trial. The court disagreed and held that at the conclusion of the jury selection process defense counsel expressly stated that the jury was acceptable to the defense. Defendant therefore abandoned the objection to the composition of the jury that she had previously made in the pre-trial motion. The court also held that the exclusion of the jurors opposed to capital punishment did not deprive defendant of her constitutional right to an impartial jury at the guilt or innocence phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Evans v. State


Nos. 66, 98, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 487; 499 A.2d 1261; 1985 Md. LEXIS 882



November 12, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at United States v. Grandison, 780 F.2d 425, 1985 U.S. App. LEXIS 25032 (4th Cir. Md., 1985)
Reconsideration denied by Foster v. State, 305 Md. 306, 503 A.2d 1326, 1986 Md. LEXIS 183 (1986)
Later proceeding at Grandison v. State, 305 Md. 685, 506 A.2d 580, 1986 Md. LEXIS 217 (1986)
Writ of certiorari denied Evans v. Maryland, 478 U.S. 1010, 106 S. Ct. 3310, 92 L. Ed. 2d 722, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 2664, 54 U.S.L.W. 3860 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Worcester County Dale R. Cathell, Judge
Grandison v. Maryland, 470 U.S. 1034, 105 S. Ct. 1411, 84 L. Ed. 2d 795, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 1335, 53 U.S.L.W. 3635 (1985)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for first-degree murder and his death sentence in the Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland). Defendant argued that pretrial identification of him by two witnesses was coercive, that witnesses who testified against defendant at trial were incompetent to testify, and that defendant was not the sole proximate cause of the victims' death, as he was hired to murder, and thus the sentence was improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a murder-for-hire plot of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant sought review of the conviction and sentence, arguing that the pretrial identification by witnesses of him was coercive, that the witnesses who testified against him at trial were incompetent to testify due to previous commissions of perjury, that the prosecutor improperly used preemptory strikes to exclude blacks from the jury, and that the fact that the murder was committed for hire was a mitigating fact pursuant to Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 413(g)(6), as defendant was not the sole proximate cause of death, and thus the death sentence was improper. The court affirmed the murder conviction and the death sentence, stating that Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 413 (g)(6) required the jurors to find mitigating circumstances, in deciding death penalty cases, when a defendant was not the sole proximate cause of the victim's death. However, the words "proximate cause" applied only to direct physical causes of death, and not to the acts of a principal in the second degree. Thus, the fact that a murder was performed pursuant to a contract was not a mitigating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and his corresponding death sentence. The words "proximate cause" applied only to the direct physical causes of the victim's death, and not to the acts of a principal in the second degree or an accessory before the fact which aided or abetted the act directly causing the death. Thus, there was nothing mitigating about the fact that defendant committed his murder for payment.

Whiting-Turner Contracting Co. v. Coupard


No. 12 (Adv.), September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 340; 499 A.2d 178; 1985 Md. LEXIS 902



October 23, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee injured person filed an action against appellants, an owner, a tenant, a builder, and an architect. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) granted summary judgment in the architect's favor on the injured person's claim against him. The builder, owner, and tenant appealed. The court issued the writ of certiorari on its own motion prior to consideration of the case by the Court of Special Appeals.


OVERVIEW: The builder, owner, and tenant contended that the 10-year limitation of Md. Code Ann. § 5-108(b) violated the guarantee of equal protection of the laws under both the United States and Maryland Constitutions, the prohibition against special laws in Md. Const. art. III, § 33, the provisions of Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. XIX, and the requirement in Md. Const. art. III, § 29 that a legislative bill embraced but one subject. The court stated that the builder, owner, and tenant had not attempted to prove and did not suggest that any particular identified design professionals were the intended beneficiaries of the enactment of Md. Code Ann. § 5-108(b). It was not a law for a special, or particular, or individual case. Hence, Md. Const. art. III, § 33 had not been violated. The court found that Md. Code Ann. § 5-108(b) did not violate Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. XIX. In the court's equal protection analysis, the court showed the reasonableness of the purpose of Md. Code Ann. § 5-108(b) and the reasonableness of the relationship of the restriction to that purpose. The court held that the bill was germane to the single subject of time bar against claims arising out of injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Cubbage v. State


No. 5, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 237; 498 A.2d 632; 1985 Md. LEXIS 909



October 9, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED AS ABOVE SET FORTH. CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS. COSTS TO ABIDE THE RESULT IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state moved to dismiss defendant's appeal of his conviction for second-degree rape and third-degree sexual assault. Defendant had waived his right to appeal in exchange for a favorable sentence. The intermediate appellate court certified the question.


OVERVIEW: After his conviction for second-degree rape and third-degree sexual assault, defendant waived his right to appeal in exchange for a more favorable sentence. Defendant then appealed to the intermediate appellate court, questioning his waiver of a jury trial and the sufficiency of the evidence to convict. The question was certified to the court. The court held that defendant could waive his right to appeal in exchange for a favorable sentence. The right to appeal a criminal conviction was statutory, not constitutional, and could be waived. A waiver of appeal was an aspect of plea bargaining. There was no state policy against the knowing and voluntary waiver of the right of appeal. The trial judge, through a full explanation to and examination of defendant, satisfied himself and developed on the record that his waiver of appeal was knowing and voluntary. There was a factual basis for a guilty plea. The court found defendant guilty after a full trial on the merits. The court dismissed the appeal, which the defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant's appeal of his criminal conviction should be dismissed where he knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to appeal.

 

258 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Fagan v. Howard County


No. 9, September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


304 Md. 250; 498 A.2d 639; 1985 Md. LEXIS 910



October 9, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY COLUMBIA PARK AND RECREATION ASSOCIATION, INC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to test the validity of statutes affecting the assessed valuation of real estate, plaintiff owners challenged a judgment of the trial court dismissing the action against defendants, a membership corporation and government officials, for lack of a proper governmental entity. The court granted certiorari prior to decision by the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), to decide the issue of terminating a collusive action before trial.


OVERVIEW: The membership corporation caused the owners in a planned community to file a test action against it, a county, and government officials, seeking a declaration of the validity of legislation that affected the computation of real estate assessments. The trial court appointed counsel for the owners and ordered the membership corporation to pay the attorney's fees and costs. When the county was dismissed from the action, the trial court dismissed the case for lack of a proper governmental entity. The owners appealed through appointed counsel, and the court granted a writ of certiorari to decide when it was proper to terminate a collusive action without adjudication. It noted that the party financing a test case was not required to continue to finance it once it decided that it was no longer interested in obtaining a judicial determination of an issue. Thus, when the membership corporation decided to cease financing the litigation against itself, all counsel should have obtained orders from the trial court terminating the appointment of counsel and the order to pay fees and costs and dismissing the action without prejudice. As the case was moot, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Broadwater v. State


No. 11, (Adv.), September Term, 1985


Court of Appeals of Maryland


303 Md. 461; 494 A.2d 934; 1985 Md. LEXIS 613



July 15, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals Bruce C. Williams, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO ABIDE THE RESULT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, prospective state senate candidate, sought a declaratory judgment against appellee state that a proposed constitutional amendment making persons who were not registered voters ineligible to serve in an elective office conflicted with the state constitution. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) dismissed the complaint with prejudice and the prospective candidate challenged that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The prospective candidate was convicted of a felony, and was disqualified to be registered as a voter under state law. The state sought to amend the constitution so that persons who were not registered voters were ineligible to serve in an elective office. Previously, while candidates for nomination at a party primary had to be registered voters, candidates seeking by petition to appear on the ballot did not. The state sought to dismiss the complaint for failure to state a claim. The trial court denied the prospective candidate's motion to amend his complaint and dismissed the complaint with prejudice. The prospective candidate appealed from the decision and the court issued a writ of certiorari on its own motion so that it could address the issue. The court vacated the judgment and held that (1) a demurrer, the type of motion to dismiss here involved, was rarely appropriate in a declaratory judgment action; (2) it was only where the declaration did not present a justiciable issue that a demurrer was appropriate; and (3) the trial court erred in failing to declare the rights of the parties even though that declaration might have been contrary to the prospective candidate's desires.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment dismissing the action and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

260 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 40, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


303 Md. 323; 493 A.2d 1062; 1985 Md. LEXIS 603



June 12, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County - Judge James S. McAuliffe) JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was charged with theft in violation of Md. Code Ann. of 1957 Art. 27, § 344(a). The defendant filed a motion for a bill of particulars and to dismiss the charges based on his belief that the state failed to allege the elements of the substantive offense in the indictment. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the trial court's ruling that denied the defendant's motion to dismiss. The defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The defendant contended that because of the wide variety of elements that comprise the crime of theft under Md. Code Ann. of 1957 art. 27, § 342, the charging document, which merely stated that the defendant "stole" specified property of the named victim, did not sufficiently inform him of the essential elements of the crime with which he was charged. Thus, he argued that the charging document was not in compliance with the standards of Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 21 and the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the Federal Constitution. The court held that the charging document was specific enough to apprise the defendant of the offense he was accused of committing. In so holding, the court found that 1) all essential elements of the crime needed not be expressly averred in the charging document; 2) the short form indictment did not violate the defendant's constitutional rights under the state or federal constitutions; 3) the charge that the defendant "did steal" the personal property of a specified victim properly characterized theft under § 342; and) the trial court should have granted the defendant's request for a bill of particulars.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the charges against him for lack of specificity in the charging document.

Lodowski v. State


Nos. 154, September Term 1983, 1, September Term 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


302 Md. 691; 490 A.2d 1228; 1985 Md. LEXIS 577



April 23, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Charles County Jacob S. Levin, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CHARLES COUNTY FOR A NEW TRIAL; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland) of first-degree murder and robbery and was convicted by the court of conspiracy related to the murders and robbery. The court sentenced him to death on one murder conviction, three consecutive life sentences and two consecutive 20-year sentences on other offenses, and held that three counts were merged. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two lawyers hired by defendant's mother went to the police station where police refused to allow them to see defendant because he had waived his right to counsel. Police did not advise defendant of the presence of the lawyers until after he had signed an incriminating statement, his third to police, which defendant sought to suppress. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's challenge to the validity of the indictment alleging that the grand jury was not representative of a cross section of the community and his argument that removal from Prince George's County to Charles County denied him equal protection of the law. However, the court held that the third statement was involuntary and inadmissible because he was denied his Fifth and Fourteenth Amendment right to the assistance of counsel. The improper admission of the third statement tainted defendant's earlier statements and made them inadmissible. Because the statements were considered by the trier of fact in both trials, a reversal of all judgments and a new trial were required. The rulings on the validity of the indictment, the removal to Charles County, and the admissibility of the third statement were law of the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of conviction and remanded the case to Charles County for a new trial. Costs were assessed to Prince George's County.

Baltimore Lutheran High School Asso. v. Employment Sec. Admin.

Ann. Code art. 95A, § 20(g)(7)(v)B for employees of an organization operated primarily for religious purposes. An exemption was granted for employees who qualified as ministers under § 20(g)(7)(v)C. 263 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Himmighoefer v. Medallion Industries, Inc.


No. 87, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


302 Md. 270; 487 A.2d 282; 1985 Md. LEXIS 538



February 5, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County - Judge G. R. Hovey Johnson) JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; APPELLEE TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two appellant homeowners were granted a writ of certiorari to challenge a decision from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County(Maryland), which held that they had constructive notice of appellee subcontractor's petitions to establish a mechanic's lien on their property and that the liens be entered against each property.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the time the petitions for the liens were filed each appellant couple had signed a contract to purchase a house in the development where the subcontractor had furnished work and materials. The sales contracts were not recorded and the homeowners were not given notice when the subcontractor filed petitions for the liens. On appeal, the court held that under the new mechanic's lien law, the subcontractor's action could place it in no better position than that which would have prevailed had it obtained a judgment against the seller between the time of the contracts of sale and the passing of the deeds. The homeowners were vested with equitable title prior to the filing of the petition for a mechanics' lien. The subcontractor's petition could create no lien because a lien only came into being upon court order. The interest of the homeowners in the land in question could not be reached by the mechanics' liens.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which imposed a mechanic's lien on the properties sold to the homeowners.

Prince George's Doctors' Hospital, Inc. v. Health Services Cost Review Com.


No. 99, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


302 Md. 193; 486 A.2d 744; 1985 Md. LEXIS 533



January 16, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals David Ross, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY ITS OWN COSTS INCLUDING COSTS OF RECORD EXTRACT; CROSS-APPELLANT TO PAY ALL COSTS OF APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which upheld an order of appellee Health Services Cost Review Commission that set appellant's rates lower than what appellant had requested and that found appellant had overcharged its patients. Appellee insurer also challenged the amount of rates ordered alleging they were too generous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital requested patient rates that would have generated an excess of $ 41.5 million in gross revenue per year. Appellee Health Services Cost Review Commission entered an order approving rates for the hospital that would have generated $ 35.1 million in gross revenue and that found the hospital had overcharged its patients when it had placed its requested rates into effect. A lower appellate upheld the order. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that the commission did not exceed its authority by imposing a guaranteed inpatient revenue system where pursuant to Md. Code. Ann., Health-Gen. § 19-216(c), it was empowered to approve alternative methods or rate determination that were experimental in nature for promoting efficient use of health care services. The court held the commission did not exceed its power by attempting to regulate ancillary services because the technical component of the ancillary services had been traditionally included in the bills submitted to the patients and were regarded as a part of the total costs. The court concluded the set rates were not confiscatory where the hospital could receive a fair return on the value of its assets.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that upheld an order of Health Services Cost Review Commission that set a hospital's rates and that found the hospital had overcharged its patients.

 

265 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Automobile Trade Asso. v. Harold Folk Enterprises, Inc.


No. 97, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 642; 484 A.2d 612; 1984 Md. LEXIS 398



December 7, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied January 7, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSED AND REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR AN ENTRY OF A JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE APPORTIONED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee automobile referral sales business (business) filed a declaratory judgment action against appellant Motor Vehicle Administration of Maryland (MVA), seeking injunctive and mandamus relief. Appellant association of new automobile dealers intervened in the action. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) ordered that the MVA was required to renew the licenses of the business' referral agents. The MVA appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an agreement between the business and participating dealers, the business' referral agents arranged the sales of new vehicles and the dealers sold the vehicle to the customer at a discounted price and paid the business a referral fee. The MVA refused to renew the licenses of the business' referral agents on the ground that the referral agents did not meet certain licensure requirements. The court held that (1) the business was not required to file a cross-appeal in order to present its arguments to the court because the business received a judgment wholly in its favor at trial; (2) by referring a customer to a specific dealer, the referral agents induced or attempted to induce the sale of a vehicle between that dealer and that customer within the meaning of Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 15-101(e)(ii) (1984 Repl. Vol.); and (3) the referral agents were employees of the business, not employees of the dealers, under Md. Code Ann., Transp. I § 15-101(e)(ii) (1984 Repl. Vol.), which prohibited dual employment. Thus, the court held that the business' referral agents were vehicle salesmen and were required to comply with the applicable licensure requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded for entry of a judgment that was consistent with the court's opinion.

 

266 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Goldstein v. Time-Out Family Amusement Centers, Inc.


No. 47, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 583; 483 A.2d 1276; 1984 Md. LEXIS 393



November 28, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals James L. Wray JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY WITH DIRECTION TO DISMISS THE BILL OF COMPLAINT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant comptroller sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which denied its demurrer to appellee family amusement center's bill of complaint for declaratory judgment against the comptroller seeking a declaration that the implementing regulations for an amusement admission tax, Md. Regs. Code tit. 03, § 01.01.01., was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The family amusement center filed a bill of complaint challenging the constitutionality of an admissions and amusement tax. The comptroller filed a demurrer asserting that the center failed to exhaust all administrative remedies. The court stated that in order to come within the "constitutional attack" exception to the general rule concerning the exhaustion of administrative remedies, the attack must have been made to the constitutionality of the statute as a whole and not merely as to how the statute had been applied. The court found that the constitutional attack by the center was not to the statute as a whole. The court stated that its protest was limited to the statutory exemptions granted to recreational businesses, and not upon the exemptions for non-profit and charity institutions. The court found that the center had to exhaust its administrative remedies before seeking a judicial determination. The court held that the trial court erred in denying the comptroller's demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to dismiss the bill of complaint.

 

267 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Vytar Associates v. Annapolis


No. 117, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 558; 483 A.2d 1263; 1984 Md. LEXIS 387



November 27, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Martin A. Wolff, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTION TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE MARYLAND TAX COURT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY MAYOR AND ALDERMEN OF THE CITY OF ANNAPOLIS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which reversed the decision of the tax court ordering appellee city to refund certain license fees that were ruled unconstitutional. The circuit court found that the retrospective provision of emergency legislation that gave the city the power to impose the fees was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the court ruled that the city's licensing powers, in which the owners paid fees to the city, violated the state constitution, the legislature enacted emergency legislation giving the city the power to charge the license fee, and made the legislation retroactive. The owners applied to the city for a refund pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 215. When the city denied the refund request, the owners appealed to the tax court, which found in their favor. But the circuit court reversed the ruling. The court heard the appeal on its own motion for certiorari and reversed the circuit court's decision, holding that, to the extent the new legislation applied retrospectively to authorize imposition of the license fees paid by the owners, the legislation was invalid as impairing property rights in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 24. The court found that the legislature could not have taken away the owners' right to recover money that was due them when the legislature passed the new laws. And the attempt to change the legislative policy under the guise of curative acts was impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's reversal of the tax court's ruling that the owners were entitled to a refund of license fees that they had unconstitutionally paid to the city.

 

268 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Faulkner


No. 47, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 482; 483 A.2d 759; 1984 Md. LEXIS 389



November 21, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Criminal Court of Baltimore - Judge Basil A. Thomas). JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed defendant's convictions for assault with intent to murder and related handgun offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot the victim during the course of a fight, believing that the victim had a knife. The trial court instructed the jury with regard to self-defense, but declined to instruct the jury on imperfect self-defense as requested by defendant. On appeal, the court agreed with the appeals court and held that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury as to the defense of imperfect self-defense. The court held: (1) the mitigation defense of imperfect self-defense was necessarily raised when defendant generated the issue of justification or excuse by way of perfect self-defense; (2) the mitigation defense of imperfect self-defense applied to the statutory crime of assault with intent to murder under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 12 (1957); and (3) the trial court should have granted defendant's requested instruction on imperfect self-defense because defendant produced sufficient evidence to generate a jury issue as to whether he had a subjectively honest but objectively unreasonable belief that he was in imminent danger of death or serious bodily injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeals court's reversal of defendant's convictions.

 

269 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


American Trucking Assos. v. Goldstein


No. 108, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 372; 483 A.2d 47; 1984 Md. LEXIS 375



November 1, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals Bruce C. Williams, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. PETITIONERS TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a trucking association and individual motor carriers, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which, in an action against defendant officials, held that a commercial vehicle registration fee under Md. Code Ann. art. 81, § 423(a) did not violate the Commerce Clause, the Equal Protection Clause, the Privileges and Immunities Clause, and the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Under Md. Code Ann. art. 81, 423(a) (1957) (Act), an annual fee was imposed on all commercial motor vehicles operated by a motor carrier, regardless of whether they were titled in Maryland or elsewhere. The association and the carriers filed an action against the officials, seeking a declaration that the fee violated the United States Constitution. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the officials, declaring that the Act was constitutional. The court granted a writ for certiorari and affirmed the judgment. The court held that (1) the Act did not violate the Commerce Clause because there was a substantial nexus between the annual fee and the state's interest, and the interstate movement of commercial vehicles on state highways afforded an adequate basis for imposition of taxes needed to support the state's highway system; the fee did not discriminate against interstate commerce or violate the Equal Protection Clause; (2) the Act did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause, which was inapplicable to corporations; and (3) the Act did not violate the Supremacy Clause because state law was not preempted by Interstate Commerce Commission regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the officials, and against the association and the carriers.

 

270 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. State


Nos. 151, September Term, 1982, 44, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 294; 483 A.2d 6; 1984 Md. LEXIS 369



October 31, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County Cullen H. Hormes, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of two first-degree murders, rape, two first-degree sexual offenses, and armed robbery, and which sentenced him to death for one of the murders and life imprisonment and a 20-year consecutive sentences for the remaining convictions.


OVERVIEW: The court found no ground for reversal of the convictions or sentences. Proof of the victim's violent character was properly excluded because defendant failed to establish an issue of self-defense before he sought to introduce that evidence. Any error in the refusal to strike jurors for cause was waived when defendant indicated that the jury was acceptable. The trial court's calling of defendant's brother as a witness was not an abuse of discretion in light of the circumstances and the limitation of the questioning. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction for the first-degree sexual offense. Objections to the psychiatric testimony in the penalty phase were not based on constitutional grounds, but in any event, there was no violation of defendant's constitutional rights. The trial court's rulings with respect to mitigating and aggravating circumstances were proper. The trial court's proportionality review under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 414(e)(4) properly found that the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate. All of the challenges to the constitutionality of the capital punishment law were previously rejected in a cited case.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentences including the death sentence were affirmed.

 

271 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Howard County v. JJM, Inc.


No. 140, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 256; 482 A.2d 908; 1984 Md. LEXIS 367



October 25, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied December 3, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Raymond J. Kane, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; HOWARD COUNTY TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee developer submitted a subdivision plan with residential lots within a right-of-way for the proposed relocation of a state route. Because the plan did not comply with Howard County, Md., Code § 16.113(b)(2) that such road right-of-ways be reserved, appellant county did not approve it. The local planning appeals board affirmed, but the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland) reversed. The county sought review.


OVERVIEW: The county argued that the reservation of a right-of-way in a subdivision for a proposed state road constituted a valid exercise of police power and was not an unconstitutional taking of property without compensation. The county further argued that the ordinance did not deprive the developer of all beneficial use of the property and that possible diminution in value of the property did not render the regulation a taking. The developer asserted that Howard County, Md., Code § 16.113(b)(2) constituted an unconstitutional taking of property without compensation because there was no time limitation on the reservation of the property and there were no benefits or payments to the developer. The court affirmed that § 16.113(b)(2) constituted an unconstitutional taking and not merely a valid exercise of police power. The court found that the ordinance could be upheld if there was a reasonable nexus between the exaction and the proposed subdivision. Because the duration of the reservation was unlimited and did not permit the developer any effective use of the property placed in reservation, the court held that the ordinance constituted an unconstitutional taking without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that the ordinance was an unconstitutional taking of the developer's property.

State ex rel. Attorney Gen. v. Burning Tree Club, Inc.


No. 138, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 9; 481 A.2d 785; 1984 Md. LEXIS 354



October 2, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Calvin R. Sanders, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Attorney General sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which sustained appellee country club's demurrer. Appellant brought a declaratory action challenging the constitutionality of a statute that provided an exemption from the prohibition against sexual discrimination for country clubs operated with the purpose of serving or benefiting members of a particular sex.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Attorney General filed a declaratory action challenging the constitutionality of a statute that provided an exemption from the prohibition against sexual discrimination for country clubs operated with the purpose of benefiting members of a particular sex. The trial court granted appellee country club's demurrer, and the court affirmed. The court held that the pendency of another similar case did not render the proceeding moot. The court held that the Attorney General did not fit within the dilemma doctrine because he was not faced with an action in tort, removal from office, or any "greater penalty" for his actions under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 19(e)(4). The court found that the Attorney General's common law powers did not enable him to bring the action, that he was not granted express authority to initiate the action, and that the action was not within his constitutional or statutory powers. The court held that because the Attorney General had the duty of appearing as the defender of the validity of enactments of the General Assembly, he could not maintain the proceeding, which sought to have an act of the General Assembly declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to sustain appellee country club's demurrer in appellant Attorney General's declaratory action challenging the constitutionality of a statute that provided an exemption from the prohibition against sexual discrimination for country clubs operated with the purpose of serving or benefiting members of a certain sex. The court held that the Attorney General did not have standing to challenge the statute.

White v. State


Nos. 20, 82, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 719; 481 A.2d 201; 1984 Md. LEXIS 342



September 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County John E. Raine, Jr. JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which convicted him of capital murder and other offenses and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed the victim during an attempt to rob the victim of the moped he was riding. Within one-half hour of the shooting, defendant and his accomplice were arrested nearby. Defendant was convicted by a jury of capital murder and other offenses and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court held, inter alia, that: (1) any error in the denial of defendant's challenge for cause of a prospective juror was waived by defense counsel's pronouncement that the jury was acceptable; (2) statements made to a third party were not within the ambit of disclosure required by Md. R. 741(a)(2), so there was no violation of that rule by the state; (3) in light of the trial court's prompt and firm intervention when the state referred to impermissible matters, there was no abuse of discretion in denying a mistrial, (4) the jury could rationally have concluded that defendant's youthful age was not a mitigating factor; (5) defendant's objection to a parole agent's testimony was properly overruled; and (6) considering both the crime and the defendant, the sentence of death was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of capital murder and other offenses and sentenced him to death.

Sites v. State


No. 148, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 702; 481 A.2d 192; 1984 Md. LEXIS 340



September 12, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied October 1, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Howard County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. J. Thomas Nissel JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted certiorari review of an order of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland) that denied his pretrial motion to suppress the results of a chemical sobriety test that defendant consented to take after he was stopped by the police for drunk driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was apprehended for drunk driving and read a statement of his rights and the penalties for refusal to submit to a chemical sobriety test. Defendant agreed to take a sobriety test and signed the required consent form. At the police station, defendant alleged that he made several requests to speak with his attorney before the test was administered. Defendant was told that he had no right to counsel, and the test was administered. In arguing his pretrial motion to suppress the results, defendant claimed that he was denied his statutory and constitutional right to counsel prior to the administration of the test. The trial court ruled that defendant had no right to counsel, and defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. Certiorari review was granted, and the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that due process required that defendant have a reasonable opportunity to communicate with his counsel before the sobriety test only if the communication did not interfere with the timely and efficacious administration of the testing process. Given the attendant delay that would have resulted in this case, defendant's due process rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence of a chemical sobriety test at his criminal trial.

 

275 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Widgeon v. Eastern Shore Hospital Center


Misc. No. 5, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 520; 479 A.2d 921; 1984 Md. LEXIS 338



August 21, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certification of Question of Law from the U.S. District Court, District of Maryland. Edward S. Northrop, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: QUESTION ANSWERED AS HEREIN SET FORTH. COSTS IN THIS COURT TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon certification from the U.S. District Court, District of Maryland, the court, pursuant to the Uniform Certification of Questions of Law Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 12-601 through 12-609 (1974), was asked to answer the question as to whether a private cause of action for damages existed for violations of articles 24 and 26 of Maryland Declaration of Rights, Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 24 and 26.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action in federal district court pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and other common law actions against defendant doctors and hospital for violating his rights pursuant to the Maryland Declaration of Rights (Declaration), Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 24 and 26. He was involuntarily committed as mentally ill solely on the perjured testimony of his wife, who did so in order to run off with her new boyfriend. The district court certified the question to the court under the Uniform Certification of Questions of Law Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 12-601 through 12-609 (1974), as to whether art. 24 and 26 created a private right of action for damages. The court answered in the affirmative based on the history of the Declaration and English common-law. The court was careful not to rule on the defenses of sovereign immunity, Amendment 11 concerns, the validity of the alternate causes of action, or whether the plaintiff had complied with procedural prerequisites, as those questions were not before it pursuant to the § 12-601 certification or dealt with federal law matters better left to the federal district court.


OUTCOME: The court answered in the affirmative the question certified to it by the federal district court pursuant to the Uniform Certification of Questions of Law Act, holding that where an individual is deprived of his liberty or property interests in violation of articles 24 and 26 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights, he may enforce those rights by bringing a common law action for damages.
