County Executive of Prince George's County v. Doe


No. 140, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 445; 479 A.2d 352; 1984 Md. LEXIS 326



August 20, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Howard S. Chasanow, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY REVERSED. COSTS TO BE EQUALLY DIVIDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county officials sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which awarded attorney fees to appellees, medical staff and related individuals.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidation action, the medical staff and related individuals sought declaratory and injunctive relief against the county officials because a county executive issued an executive order prohibiting abortions. The circuit court declared the order null and void and enjoined its enforcement, holding that the county executive lacked authority under the county charter to issue the order. The county officials appealed to the Court of Special Appeals. The court issued a writ of certiorari prior to a decision by the intermediate appellate court, and affirmed the declaratory judgment and injunction, but did not address the claims under 42 U.S.C.S. §1983. The medical staff and individuals filed a motion for attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, which the circuit court granted. On appeal, the court reversed. The 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim failed to meet the federal standards for an attorney fee award under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 because the federal issue raised was wholly insubstantial. The U.S. Constitution did not require a state or local government to provide nontherapeutic abortion services at a hospital owned and operated by the government.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of attorney fees in favor of the medical staff and related individuals and against the county officials.

Trimble v. State


Nos. 15, 98, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 387; 478 A.2d 1143; 1984 Md. LEXIS 328



August 17, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County Cullen H. Hormes, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) convicted defendant of first-degree murder, first-degree rape, first-degree sexual offense, kidnapping, and assault. He was 17 years, eight months old at the time of the offense. Insanity was his defense. He elected to be sentenced by the trial court and was sentenced to death. The entire case was before the court under to the automatic-review provision, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 414(a).


OVERVIEW: The court held (1) the trial court properly found that defendant generated an insanity issue (2) trial court's failure to include mental retardation in the jury instruction was not cause for reversal because it was not preserved for review and was not plain error, (3) defense counsel created the issue of defendant's prescription for thorazine, and could not have been heard to complain that the state sought to rebut its significance, (4) the state's attorney was permitted to call defendant's expert witness "unqualified," (5) the trial judge neither considered impermissible factors nor misapplied Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413, (5) the accused shouldered the burden of persuasion to show a somewhat broader form of insanity in sentencing proceedings, (6) the Eighth Amendment did not shield defendant, because of his age, from capital punishment, (7) the death sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, (8) the trial court had a sound basis to find the aggravating factors were not outweighed by the mitigating factors, and (9) the defendant's sentence was proportionate notwithstanding the lesser sentences received by his accomplices.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences, including the death penalty.

Moon v. State


No. 87, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 354; 478 A.2d 695; 1984 Md. LEXIS 324



July 19, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Carroll County - Judge Luke K. Burns, Jr.) JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY AND REMAND TO THAT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. CARROLL COUNTY TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Special Appeals, Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland) which determined that because of the objective nature of defendant's blood alcohol and osmolality test, they were not in violation of his constitutional rights to confrontation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after he killed two people while driving under the influence. Blood alcohol and osmolality tests were given by the hospital while he was being treated.. He contended that his right to confrontation and cross-examination was violated by admitting the tests without presenting the testimony of the technician who performed them. The court had previously determined that Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 10-302 to 10-309 did not specifically apply to the proceedings where blood was taken from defendant as part of his treatment rather than for criminal proceedings. On appeal, the court held that its previous decision secured to defendant his right to confrontation and was consistent with the policy that accorded alcohol test results less deference than other business records. The court determined that because defendant was denied the right to be confronted with the technician, it was questionable whether the report was properly admitted as a business record. The court reversed the decision and remanded because it could make no accurate assessment of the documents reliability since the means of testing trustworthiness were withheld from defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the reviewing court and remanded to the reviewing court for it to reverse the judgment of the trial court and remand to the trial court for a new trial.

Anne Arundel County v. Burnopp


No. 142, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 343; 478 A.2d 315; 1984 Md. LEXIS 323



July 16, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. H. Chester Goudy, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; APPELLEES TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which dismissed the county's petition to condemn land for a road, apparently on the grounds both of a failure to prove public necessity as well as public use.


OVERVIEW: The county sought to condemn a portion of appellee landowners' property in order to make improvements so that necessary services could be provided to certain residences. At trial, the county introduced evidence of the adoption of the appropriate resolutions for condemnation. On review, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that there was not the slightest evidence that the decision to condemn the land in question was so oppressive, arbitrary or unreasonable as to suggest bad faith. The court determined that the road, when completed, would be just as much a part of the public road system of the county as any other road in that county. The public would be entitled to use it to go to and from the businesses and residences located on it. The court held that the trial judge erred when he found that the road here was not for a public use.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the county's petition to condemn land was reversed and the case remanded.

 

280 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Parrott v. State


Misc. No. 3, September Term, 1984


Court of Appeals of Maryland


301 Md. 411; 483 A.2d 68; 1984 Md. LEXIS 376



July 10, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Per Curiam November 2, 1984. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pusuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals William H. McCullough, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an interlocutory order of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which, at the suggestion of the state, removed defendant's capital murder case in literal compliance with Md. Const. art. IV, § 8. The state moved to dismiss defendant's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the state's motion to dismiss defendant's appeal. The court held that the order of removal appealed from was not a final judgment and did not fall within the collateral order doctrine. According to the court, the removal order was not within a class of orders that granted or denied an absolute constitutional right. Therefore, the order was not immediately appealable on that ground. Furthermore, the court held that the matter was not fully disposed of by the trial court, was not separable from rights asserted in the action, and there was no risk of important loss in present review was denied.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's interlocutory appeal of the removal order of the trial court.

Vournas v. Montgomery County


No. 13, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 123; 476 A.2d 705; 1984 Md. LEXIS 303



June 22, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County - Judge Philip M. Fairbanks) JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner transferor appealed a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed a judgment of the trial court entered in favor of respondent county in a declaratory judgment action. The transferor sought to have Montgomery County, Md., Code § 52-21(d), which imposed a tax on the transfer of real property to the United States as a result of condemnation, declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The United States condemned real estate belonging to the transferor. Section 52-21(d) imposed a tax on the transferor for the transfer of the property to the United States. The lower courts held that the ordinance was constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) the court could consider events occurring subsequent to the statute's enactment when considering the scope of the statute; (2) 42 U.S.C.S. § 4653 established that a transfer of real property to the United States as a result of condemnation was not immune from local transfer taxes assessed against the owner of the condemned property; (3) the transfer tax was intended to encompass circumstances and conditions which did not exist at the time of its enactment, including the ability to tax the transfer of property to the United States; and (4) the transferor was liable to pay the tax on the transfer of the condemned property to the United States.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of special appeals entered in favor of the county in the transferor's declaratory judgment action.

 

282 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baylin v. State Rds. Com.


No. 113, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


300 Md. 1; 475 A.2d 1155; 1984 Md. LEXIS 298



June 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 2 Appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. James S. Sfekas, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED. CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. APPELLEES TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which ruled that defendant state road commission (commission) could take the property owner's land without any enhancement to its value based on the taking of additional land for an expansion to the proposed transportation project.


OVERVIEW: The commission committed to a highway construction project that required the state to condemn 19 acres from the property owner's predecessor-in-interest. Based on this commitment, the property owner purchased a larger tract of land from the predecessor-in-interest. After the purchase, and approximately 30 years after the commission committed to the project, the state substantially enlarged the project to require the condemnation of 137 acres owned by the property owner. At trial, the commission argued that none of the land taken should be appraised in light of any value added by the project as originally conceived, which position the trial court adopted. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that for purposes of just compensation under the Fifth Amendment, the property owner was entitled to the value added by the scope of the original project for the additional acres taken because the property owner purchased the land based on the prospective advantage of the original project and could not have anticipated the expanded scope of the project years later.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had ruled that the property owner was not entitled to the added value of a highway project for condemnation purposes even though the project had been substantially expanded years later to require the taking of a much larger part of the property owner's land by the commission.

Lawrence v. A.S. Abell Co.


No. 164, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 697; 475 A.2d 448; 1984 Md. LEXIS 285; 10 Media L. Rep. 2001



May 31, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Superior Court of Baltimore City - Judge Martin B. Greenfeld) JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY IS AFFIRMED. APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mothers sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) that granted summary judgment in favor of the defendant press in the mothers' action for the invasion of privacy of their children when the press used the children's photographs in certain publications.


OVERVIEW: The mothers and their children attended a festival that was being covered by the local press. A photographer for the press asked and received permission to photograph the children to accompany an article that was being written about the festival. The pictures were published as expected. Six weeks later, the press decided to use the photographs of the children in an advertising campaign. The mothers filed a defamation action and claimed that their children's identities had been misappropriated for commercial purposes, thereby unjustly enriching the press. The mothers also claimed invasion of the children's privacy. The trial court granted the press summary judgment, and the mothers appealed. The court affirmed the judgment and found that there was no unjust enrichment because the children's photographs had no commercial or other value. The court also agreed that there was no invasion of privacy because the reproduction of the images were merely incidental.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment that was granted by the trial court in favor of the press in the mothers' defamation action.

Turner v. State


No. 79, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 565; 474 A.2d 1297; 1984 Md. LEXIS 286



May 24, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for St. Mary's County Joseph A. Mattingly, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ST. MARY'S COUNTY REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY ST. MARY'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for St. Mary's County (Maryland), which convicted her of violating the Female Sitters Law, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§152, 153 (1957).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the owner and manager of a tavern, was convicted of violating the Female Sitters Law, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§152, 153 (1957). On appeal, defendant contended that the Female Sitters Law was unconstitutional. The court reversed defendant's conviction and held that the Female Sitters Law violated the Maryland Equal Rights Amendment (ERA) and was, therefore, unconstitutional. The statute imposed different benefits and different burdens upon persons based solely upon their sex and violated the Maryland ERA. Additionally, the statute established a discriminatory classification based upon the sex of the employees and its gender-based discrimination was not severable. Defendant, as an employer, had standing to challenge the validity of the Female Sitters Law, because the statute was directed at third persons with whom the employer had a business relationship, the statute impaired the employer's relationship with her female employees, and the employer suffered an immediate injury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of violationing the Maryland Female Sitters Law.

DOT., Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Armacost


No. 153, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 392; 474 A.2d 191; 1984 Md. LEXIS 268; 15 ELR 20179; 20 ERC (BNA) 2113



May 1, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Donald J. Gilmore, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: INTERLOCUTORY INJUNCTION VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS; COSTS TO ABIDE THE FINAL RESULT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellants, Department of Health, Department of Transportation, and Motor Vehicle Administration (the State), sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland), which granted an interlocutory injunction against the State in the challenge by appellees, County Commissioners of Carroll County, town, and mayor (the County), to the Vehicle Emissions Inspection Program, Md. Code Ann., Transp. §§ 23-201 to -208.


OVERVIEW: The county challenged the constitutionality of the Maryland Vehicle Emissions Inspection Program (VEIP), Md. Code Ann., Transp. §§ 23-201 to -208. The lower court granted an interlocutory injunction prohibiting the State from enforcement of VEIP in the county. The State appealed. The court vacated the interlocutory injunction and remanded the case to the lower court. The court stated that an interlocutory injunction should not be granted unless the party seeking it demonstrated a likelihood of success on the merits. The court reasoned that the county was unlikely to succeed on the merits. The county's claims under U.S. Const. Amend. IV failed because an individual had no privacy expectation in items he knowingly exposed to the public, such as his car and its emissions. Inspection of a vehicle's emissions did not constitute a warrantless search. The county's equal protection claims failed even though the State it did not require other rural counties to do testing and certain vehicles were exempted from testing. The county's due process argument failed because the State had a legitimate interest in protecting health by reducing smog and pollution.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the interlocutory injunction granted by the lower court and remanded the case.

Stebbing v. State


Nos. 35, 103, September Term, 1981


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 331; 473 A.2d 903; 1984 Md. LEXIS 267



April 16, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied May 24, 1984.
Writ of certiorari denied Stebbing v. Maryland, 469 U.S. 900, 105 S. Ct. 276, 83 L. Ed. 2d 212, 1984 U.S. LEXIS 3973 (1984)
Related proceeding at, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Certificate of appealability denied Stebbing v. Hershberger, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 2321 (D. Md., Jan. 8, 2014)
Related proceeding at, Remanded by Stebbing v. State, 2016 Md. LEXIS 503 (Md., Aug. 17, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Harford County. Albert P. Close, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hartford County (Maryland), which convicted her of first degree murder, first degree rape, robbery, and first degree sexual assault. The trial court, upon defendant's waiver of sentencing by the jury, imposed a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: In challenging the judgment, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in prohibiting her expert medical witnesses from testifying regarding whether she had the necessary intent to commit the alleged crimes, that there was insufficient evidence to support either the robbery conviction or sexual assault convictions, and that the trial court erred in determining the aggravating and mitigating circumstances when imposing her sentence. The court found no abuse of discretion in limitations imposed on the expert testimony, noting that it was improper for an expert witness to resolve conflicts in the evidence in order to form an opinion on a material issue. With respect to the robbery conviction, the court rejected defendant's claim that both the taking of property and force elements needed to be perpetrated simultaneously. Rather, the found that where force resulted in death, as here, a taking subsequent to death met the elements of robbery. The court found no error in the mitigating or aggravating factors determined by the trial court. After mandatory review of the death sentence as required by Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 414, the court found it appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first degree murder and related offenses and her sentence of death.

State v. Good Samaritan Hospital, Inc.


No. 100, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 310; 473 A.2d 892; 1984 Md. LEXIS 266; 45 A.L.R.4th 869



April 11, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. J. Harold Grady, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Maryland (state), sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which declared that Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 19-351(b) (1982), as applied to appellee hospital, violated the Contracts Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The hospital had filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 19-351(b).


OVERVIEW: Section 19-351(b) required that any hospital that offered medical or surgical foot care must permit qualified podiatrists to obtain staff privileges and to use hospital facilities, thereby prohibiting the hospitals from categorically excluding all podiatrists. The hospital claimed that § 19-351(b) was unconstitutional as being in violation of the Contracts Clause, and the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment and the Maryland Constitution. The trial court found that § 19-351(b) violated the Contracts Clause. On appeal, the court vacated. The court found that, although the hospital's charter constituted a contract with the state, § 19-351(b) did not change or impair any contractual obligation arising out of the hospital's charter. Nothing in the charter existed which would permit the hospital to conduct its activities without regard to the enactment of legislation. Accordingly, there was no Contracts Clause violation. The hospital failed to prove that it was denied due process or equal protection of the laws, and § 19-351(b) did not constitute a special law in violation of Md. Const. art. III, § 33 because it benefitted all podiatrists equally.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the judgment of the trial court that found that the podiatry statute violated the Contracts Clause.

Kawamura v. State


No. 84, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 276; 473 A.2d 438; 1984 Md. LEXIS 263



April 9, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 3 Appeals from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. James J. McAuliffe, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY IN EQUITY NO. 78080 AND MISCELLANEOUS PETITION NO. 5855 AFFIRMED. JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY IN LAW NO. 60250 REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. MONTGOMERY COUNTY TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged and convicted of the theft of goods having a value of under $ 300. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) invoked Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 4-302(d)(2) and denied defendant a jury trial. Defendant challenged his conviction claiming that § 4-302(d)(2) was unconstitutionally applied to his case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 4-302(d)(2) was inapplicable to cases involving theft. The court agreed with defendant and reversed and remanded his conviction. The court reasoned that defendant had properly sought a writ of certiorari for the circuit court to examine the district court's denial of his request for a jury trial. Further, the court found that Md. Code Ann. Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 4-302(d)(1) expressly deprived the trial court of jurisdiction over a cause where a defendant requested and was entitled to a jury trial. Along those same lines the court found that defendant could not have been denied a trial for any criminal offense for which he was liable to infamous punishment. The court reasoned further that any confinement in prison constituted an infamous punishment. Therefore, because defendant was subject to confinement in prison for the crime of theft, he could not be denied a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for the theft of goods having a value of under $ 300.

County Comm'rs of Charles County v. Stevens


No. 94, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 203; 473 A.2d 12; 1984 Md. LEXIS 258; 20 ERC (BNA) 2080



April 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Charles County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. George W. Bowling, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CHARLES COUNTY WITH DIRECTIONS TO ENTER A PARTIAL DECLARATORY JUDGMENT ON THE COMMERCE CLAUSE ISSUE CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION, AND FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS ON THE REMAINING CONSTITUTIONAL ISSUES RAISED, BUT NOT DECIDED, BY THE CIRCUIT COURT; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE, ALBERT W. STEVENS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland), which held that the county's regulation banning disposal, in a county owned and operated landfill facility, of solid waste originating outside the county's borders violated the Commerce Clause. Appellee operator of a solid waste hauling business (operator) filed an action after the county suspended one of his permits for violating the regulation.


OVERVIEW: The operator filed a complaint seeking a declaration that Charles Co., Md., Regulation 4(d) was unconstitutional under the Commerce, Equal Protection, and Due Process Clauses and under Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 24, and an injunction barring enforcement of the regulation. The circuit court concluded that Regulation 4(d) unconstitutionally discriminated against interstate commerce because it overtly discriminated against articles in interstate commerce. On appeal, the county argued that it was entitled to legally prohibit the disposal of solid waste originating outside of the county at its landfill facility. The court held that Regulation 4(d) did not violate the Commerce Clause because the county was operating the landfill as a market participant, rather than as a market regulator, therefore, the dormant Commerce Clause did not apply to its activities. The court reasoned that Regulation 4(d) did nothing more than limit the benefits of this service to the county taxpayers who paid for it, and that it applied to only one participant in the market, its landfill facility. It did not restrict the disposal of waste collected outside of the county in any other landfill within the county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment declaring that the county's regulation banning disposal in its landfill of solid waste originating outside of the county violated the Commerce Clause, remanded the case with directions for the circuit court to enter a partial declaratory judgment on the Commerce Clause issue, and ordered the circuit court to conduct further proceedings on the remaining constitutional issues.

Colvin v. State


Nos. 84, 114, September Term, 1981


Court of Appeals of Maryland


299 Md. 88; 472 A.2d 953; 1984 Md. LEXIS 235



March 16, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. E. Mackall Childs, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 414, defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which convicted him of the felony murder of an 82-year-old woman during a burglary and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his murder conviction and the death penalty imposed for the brutal stabbing of an 82-year-old woman during a burglary. Latent fingerprints, lifted from a broken glass door, were matched with known prints of defendant and he later pawned jewelry stolen from the home. Defendant claimed error in the denial of his motion to suppress certain evidence, and asserted that the trial court erred in failing to conduct a proper inquiry after he sought to waive counsel. Defendant also challenged the constitutionally of the state's death penalty statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413(e)(1), claiming his death sentence was based on the same evidence of felony murder. After a mandatory review of the sentence pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 414(e)(4), the appellate court affirmed the conviction and sentence because the imposition of a sentence of death in a felony murder case was not necessarily excessive and unconstitutional. Finding no error in the trial court's evidentiary rulings, the appellate court held that defendant never asserted his right to self-representation and merely sought to replace the public defender with an attorney of his choice at state expense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed on the grounds that the trial court properly did not pursue the inquiry essential to determining defendant's right to proceed without counsel because defendant never made a statement from which the trial court could reasonably conclude that he desired self-representation. The death sentence was also affirmed because consideration of the underlying felony as an aggravating circumstance was proper.

Rosecroft Trotting & Pacing Asso. v. Prince George's County

March 6, 1984

The taxpayers brought an action against the county challenging its power to set two different tax rates on separate classes of property. Griffith v. Wakefield


No. 159, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


298 Md. 381; 470 A.2d 345; 1984 Md. LEXIS 211; 117 L.R.R.M. 2219



February 1, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied March 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. James S. Sfekas, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO ENTER A JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. RESPONDENT BALTIMORE COUNTY FIREFIGHTERS ASSOCIATION, LOCAL 1311, TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which granted the summary judgment motion filed by intervenor firefighters association in the taxpayers' action against defendant board of supervisors of elections (board). The taxpayers sought declaratory relief and an injunction restraining the board from placing a proposed amendment on the ballot for the general election.


OVERVIEW: The proposed amendment required resolution of labor disputes, involving county-employed fire fighters, through binding arbitration. The taxpayers argued that the amendment did not constitute "charter material" under Md. Const. art. XI-A. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment because, when viewed as a whole, the amendment did not alter the form or structure of the county government. Instead, the core of the amendment was the imposition of a comprehensive system of binding arbitration concerning a single group of county employees. The electorate, through the charter amendment process, was attempting to circumvent the local legislative body and enact local law, which was impermissible under article XI-A. The proposed charter amendment did not authorize the county council to enact binding arbitration legislation for county employees. It did not authorize any decisions by the constitutional legislative body. Therefore, the proposed amendment was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of the firefighters association in the taxpayers' action that sought to declare a proposed amendment unconstitutional was reversed.

Supervisor of Assessments v. Carroll

298 Md. 311; 469 A.2d 858; 1984 Md. LEXIS 210

CASE SUMMARY:

Ann. Code art. 81, § 19(b)(1)(1980).

The taxpayer appealed, arguing that the residences occupied by farm employees were entitled to exemption under § 19(b)(1). Potomac Electric Power Co. v. Prince George's County


No. 102, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


298 Md. 185; 468 A.2d 325; 1983 Md. LEXIS 339



December 22, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Perry G. Bowen, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE BILL OF COMPLAINT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE PLAINTIFF. MANDATE TO ISSUE FORTHWITH.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action against appellees, Prince George's County (Maryland) and related parties, to declare an ordinance and resolution unconstitutional, appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment, denying injunctive relief and upholding the validity of the ordinance. Before proceedings in the appellate court, the court granted cross-petitions for certiorari that questioned the constitutionality of different tax rates for personal and real property.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer instituted an action to declare unconstitutional an ordinance and resolution of the County that imposed different tax rates for personal property and real property. The trial court denied injunction relief and upheld the ordinance, and the taxpayer sought review. Before the appellate court took action, the court granted certiorari. The court vacated the judgment, explaining that, during oral argument, in response to questions from the court, the parties disclosed that the taxpayer had paid the full amount of the taxes for the period in controversy. It was also represented that the County had not spent the disputed funds, pending a termination of the litigation. The court held that once a taxpayer voluntarily paid a tax or other governmental charge, under a mistake of law or under what he regarded as an illegal imposition, no common law action existed for the recovery of the tax absent a special statutory provision sanctioning a refund. This was true even if payment was made under protest. It further held that the fact that the County had deferred spending the money had no legal effect.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with directions to dismiss the bill of complaint.

King v. State Rds. Com. of State Highway Admin.


No. 28, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


298 Md. 80; 467 A.2d 1032; 1983 Md. LEXIS 329



December 6, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Rosalyn B. Bell, Judge



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Maryland State Roads Commission filed a petition for a "quick-take" on appellant landowner's property for highway purposes. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) valued the property and damage to the remainder at $ 64,693 and the landowner was awarded six-percent interest from the date of the taking. The landowner appealed the trial court's denial of his motion for supplemental interest.


OVERVIEW: After the landowner received the condemnation award, he sought additional interest arguing that the six-percent interest rate authorized by Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 12-106(c) deprived him of the constitutionally mandated "just compensation" for his property. Instead, the landowner contended that he was entitled to interest at the prevailing market rate. The trial court denied the motion and found that the interest on the award was not an integral part of "just compensation." The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, but on different grounds. The court held that the interest award was an integral part of just compensation in a quick-take case and that the six-percent specified in § 12-106(c) was the minimum rate of interest to which a landowner was entitled. If the landowner produced evidence that the six-percent rate was constitutionally insufficient, he would be entitled to a higher rate of return as part of just compensation. However, the question of the proper rate was a factual determination to be made by the jury and the landowner waived his right to a higher interest rate by failing to present the issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the landowner's motion for supplemental interest.

Anthony Plumbing of Maryland, Inc. v. Attorney Gen. of Maryland


No. 158, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


298 Md. 11; 467 A.2d 504; 1983 Md. LEXIS 325



November 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Solomon Baylor, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED. APPELLANTS TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company appealed a portion of an order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which appointed a special master to take additional testimony following a trial and assessed civil penalties and costs in the plaintiff state's suit brought under the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, Md. Code Ann., Com. Law §§ 13-101 to 13-501.


OVERVIEW: After hearing extensive testimony, the trial court found that the company had engaged in unlawful practices under the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, enjoined the company from engaging in such practices, ordered payment of restitution to consumers who testified at trial, assessed civil penalties, awarded the costs of the action to the state and appointed a special master to hear testimony from other consumers allegedly victimized by the company. The court dismissed the appeal sua sponte, holding that the order appointing a special master was not a final order appealable under Md. Code. Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-301, because proceedings before the master would not have constituted a separate trial, and his findings would not have finally disposed of the litigation. Because the order for payment of costs to the state created a debt actionable at law, it was not equitable in nature and the court determined that it was not appealable as an interlocutory order under Md. Code. Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-303(c)(5). The court held that it was not vested with jurisdiction despite the consent of the parties.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the company's appeal sua sponte.

 

297 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Calhoun v. State


No. 129, September Term, 1981, No. 5, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


297 Md. 563; 468 A.2d 45; 1983 Md. LEXIS 322



November 21, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed November 30, 1983; Denied December 5, 1983.
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Calhoun, 306 Md. 692, 511 A.2d 461, 1986 Md. LEXIS 265 (1986)
Post-conviction relief denied at Calhoun-El v. State, 231 Md. App. 285, 150 A.3d 886, 2016 Md. App. LEXIS 1569 (2016)
Decision reached on appeal by Calhoun v. State, 2017 Md. App. LEXIS 104 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., Jan. 30, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Cave, J.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed directly to the court from his conviction and death penalty sentence issued by the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland). Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it allowed the introduction of hypnotically enhanced testimony and that the aggravating factors came from one incident. Defendant also attacked the constitutionality of the death penalty statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 412(b).


OVERVIEW: A policeman and two employees walked in on a robbery. A shorter assailant shot an employee. A taller assailant grabbed the policeman and pulled him into a cashroom. When the other employee was dragged into the same room, he saw that the officer received a gunshot to the head. Police interviewed a witness and the employee. Later, the police interviewed them under hypnosis; their testimony was consistent with their prior statements. At defendant's trial, an accomplice implicated defendant. The trial court denied a motion to suppress the hypnotically enhanced testimony. The jury found defendant guilty of first degree, premeditated murder. The jury found three aggravating and one mitigating factor; it sentenced him to death. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly admitted the hypnotically enhanced testimony because it was consistent with prior statements. The court found that the aggravating factors found by the jury could arise from a single incident, i.e., the murder of a police officer. The court upheld the constitutionality of the death penalty statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 412(b), on U.S. Const. amend. VIII grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentence. The court held that the trial court properly admitted hypnotically enhanced testimony of two witnesses because the enhanced testimony was not inconsistent with their prior statements to police. The court found that separate aggravating factors could arise from a single incident. The court held that the death penalty statute did not proscribe a cruel or unusual punishment.

 

298 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Tichnell v. State


No. 3, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


297 Md. 432; 468 A.2d 1; 1983 Md. LEXIS 316



November 3, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed November 30, 1983; Denied December 5, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Death Sentence (Maryland Rule 898) from the Circuit Court for Calvert County; Bowen, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court for Calvert Court (Maryland), which was entered upon the jury's verdict following the third capital sentencing hearing conducted in connection with defendant's conviction for the wilful, deliberate, and premeditated first-degree murder of a deputy sheriff.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant initially challenged the judge-conducted voir dire examination as being too limited to expose bias on the part of prospective jurors. The court noted that defendant had not identified any specific deficiencies or particular shortcomings in the judge's voir dire examination. The court therefore held that general allegations as to the judge's attitude were insufficient to demonstrate that the jury selection process failed to assure defendant of a fair and impartial jury. The court further found that defendant had received the requisite statutory notice under Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 412(b) before his original trial and that nothing in the bar of double jeopardy prevented the third capital sentencing proceeding. The court then determined that the death penalty was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, and that the evidence supported the jury's finding of aggravating factors not outweighed by mitigating circumstances. The court thus affirmed, concluding that the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases, considering both the crime and the accused.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentence imposed on defendant.

Buzbee v. Journal Newspapers, Inc.


No. 2, September Term, 1983


Court of Appeals of Maryland


297 Md. 68; 465 A.2d 426; 1983 Md. LEXIS 288; 9 Media L. Rep. 2233



September 13, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Buzbee v. State, 58 Md. App. 599, 473 A.2d 1315, 1984 Md. App. LEXIS 336 (1984)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Bell, J. Per Curiam Order Filed March 17, 1983.
Journal Newspapers, Inc. v. State, 54 Md. App. 98, 456 A.2d 963, 1983 Md. App. LEXIS 245 (1983)



DISPOSITION: This Court issued a per curiam order on March 17, 1983, affirming the intermediate appellate court and directed that the mandate should issue forthwith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certiorari, petitioner accused sought review from an order from the Court of Special Appeals for Montgomery County (Maryland) that reversed the circuit court and granted respondent publishers' request to access to a motion to suppress hearing.


OVERVIEW: The accused was charged with criminal offenses. He filed motions to suppress evidence in the criminal proceeding. The publishers intervened in the criminal proceedings seeking access to the suppression hearing. The circuit court excluded the public, including the press, from a hearing on the accused's motions to suppress certain evidence, enjoined certain classes of individuals from making extrajudicial statements concerning aspects of the criminal causes pending, and directed that certain court records be sealed. The publishers appealed. On appeal, the appellate court reversed, holding that the public's qualified right of access to criminal trials extended to pretrial judicial proceedings in criminal cases and that, on the record in the instant matter, that right was not outweighed by probable impairment of the accused's right to a fair trial. On writ of certiorari, the court affirmed the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order that reversed the circuit court and granted the publishers' request to access to a suppression hearing filed by the accused.

Office of Finance v. Previti


No. 89, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


296 Md. 512; 463 A.2d 842; 1983 Md. LEXIS 258; 38 A.L.R.4th 503



August 12, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; Langrall, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County reversed. Case remanded to that Court for the entry of a judgment affirming the judgment of the District Court of Maryland for Baltimore County. Costs to be paid by Gerald Previti.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county through certiorari sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Baltimore County (Maryland), which reversed a judgment entered in favor of the county and forfeited money seized from appellee gambler in an action seeking release of the money.


OVERVIEW: A man was arrested and his money seized, for accepting wagers on sporting events. Ultimately a stet was entered to those charges. The gambler then wrote a request for the return of his money. The request was filed as an original pleading, and the court named the county as defendant. After a hearing, the lower court forfeited the money seized. The gambler appealed the matter to the trial court which reversed the lower court. The county sought review. The court determined that Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 264 (1957), allowed for forfeiture even where the gambling charges had been dismissed. The lower court properly forfeited the money seized.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court which reversed the forfeiture allowed by the lower court, of the money seized after the gambler was arrested for accepting wagers on sporting events.

 

301 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Frick v. Maldonado


No. 23, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


296 Md. 304; 462 A.2d 1206; 1983 Md. LEXIS 274



August 4, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Levin, Jacob S., J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; appellee to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which granted a directed verdict in favor of appellee alleged father, based on the statute of limitations, in a paternity proceeding filed by the mother. The mother asserted that the two-year period of limitations found in Md. Code art. 16, § 66(e)(1973) was a denial of equal protection on the part of the child.


OVERVIEW: The child involved in this case was born on August 22, 1978, and the child's mother filed a paternity proceeding on March 20, 1981. The alleged father pleaded the statute of limitations, and the trial court granted his request for a directed verdict based on the mother's failure to meet the two-year statute of limitations period under § 66(e). The court granted certiorari and, upon review, the court reversed the judgment and overruled its earlier decision, which upheld the constitutionality of the two-year statute of limitations applicable to paternity actions. The court reviewed a number of related decisions and specifically focussed on a Tennessee statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-224(2)(1977), that was similar in content to the Maryland statute. The court agreed with the premise that the two-year period of limitations did not provide certain illegitimate children with an adequate opportunity to obtain support and was not substantially related to the legitimate state interest in preventing the litigation of stale or fraudulent claims. Thus, the court concluded that it denied certain illegitimate children the equal protection of the laws guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and overruled its prior decision regarding the constitutionality of a two-year statute of limitations applicable to paternity actions.

 

302 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Raiford v. State


No. 100, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


296 Md. 289; 462 A.2d 1192; 1983 Md. LEXIS 251



July 8, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Grady, C. J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded to that Court with instructions to affirm in part and reverse in part the judgment of the Criminal Court of Baltimore and remand for new sentencing proceeding consistent with this opinion. Costs to be paid by Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried and convicted of robbery and was sentenced to 25 years imprisonment, pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B(c). The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the conviction and sentence. The sole issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred in imposing a mandatory sentence under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B(c).


OVERVIEW: To qualify as a recidivist, the state used defendant's 1967 convictions. At the time of defendant's 1967 convictions, he was 17 years old and was tried as an adult pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 26, §§ 51-71, and Md. Ann. Code art. 4, § 240 (b). Those statutes exempted Baltimore City from the general statewide juvenile age limit of 18. This statutory exception was subsequently held to be in contravention of the equal protection and due process clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court stated that had defendant been tried as a juvenile in 1967, he would not have an adult conviction for purposes of the recidivist statute. Thus, to allow the 1967 convictions to be used to enhance his punishment under the recidivist statute constituted a present deprivation of equal protection. The court hastened to point out, however, that defendant's 1967 convictions were not declared a nullity and expunged. Because the use of the 1967 convictions to enhance defendant's punishment for his 1981 robbery conviction constituted an unconstitutional deprivation of his right to equal protection, the case was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but remanded for resentencing.

 

303 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Washington County Dep't of Social Services v. Clark


No. 142, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


296 Md. 190; 461 A.2d 1077; 1983 Md. LEXIS 246



June 23, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Washington County; Moylan, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded to the Circuit Court for Washington County for further proceedings consistent with this opinion; costs to be paid by the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Washington County Department of Social Services (department) sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland), which dismissed the department's petition for guardianship with the right to consent to adopt the five minor children of appellee mother under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 75 (1957, Repl. Vol. 1981 Supp. 1982).


OVERVIEW: After the children had been in foster care for two years, the department petitioned for guardianship with the right to consent to adopt under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 75 (1957, Repl. Vol. 1981 Supp. 1982). When a chancellor dismissed the petition, the department appealed. The court affirmed the finding that a presumption of the best interests of the children was unconstitutional. The court held that § 76(c) was unconstitutional. The law did not satisfy the mother's due process rights when it provided the clear and convincing proof to warrant termination of her parental rights by presumption. The standard was presumed when a child was in foster care for two years. The presumption violated the right to procedural due process. The court reversed the chancellor's failure to consider all factors under the statute and to appoint separate counsel for the children and remanded. The chancellor erred in not considering all the factors contained in § 76(b) for his alternative rulings. The chancellor erred in not appointing counsel for the children under § 77B(a)(4), which required counsel for persons subject to a proceeding for the involuntary termination of parental rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the chancellor's failure to consider all the factors required under the statute and to appoint separate counsel for the children and remanded to make findings of fact under the statute and to appoint separate counsel for the children in the proceedings. The court affirmed the finding that a presumption of the best interests of the children was unconstitutional.

State v. Baltimore


No. 32, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


296 Md. 67; 459 A.2d 585; 1983 Md. LEXIS 235



May 4, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed June 2, 1983; Denied June 3, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Baltimore City; Karwacki, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (now the Circuit Court for Baltimore City) reversed and case remanded to that Court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Respondent to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which entered a declaratory judgment in favor of appellees, the City of Baltimore (city), that the city was not liable for unpaid criminal court costs incurred when an accused was relieved of the obligation to pay the costs because of his indigency or because of a disposition of criminal proceedings in his favor.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the state's petition for a writ of certiorari to determine whether the city was liable for unpaid criminal court costs incurred when an accused was relieved of the obligation to pay the costs because of his indigency or because of a disposition of criminal proceedings in his favor. The trial court determined that the city was not liable for such costs under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 7-202(b), which prohibited charges against the city without its consent. The court disagreed and reversed. The court held that § 7-202(b) applied only when the city was a party to proceedings. Any other construction would have rendered Ch. 11 of the Acts of 1781, codified as Md. Ann. Code art. 38, §4A (1982), repealed by implication. The provision authorized the payment of such costs by the city. The court refused to repeal the latter statute by implication. Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 2-504 did not abrogate Md. Ann. Code art. 38, §4A. The statute of limitations in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-101 did not apply because such statutes do not run against the state. The court held that the city was liable to the state for criminal court costs and fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that the City of Baltimore was not liable for unpaid criminal court costs incurred when an accused was relieved of the obligation to pay the costs because of his indigency or because of a disposition of criminal proceedings in his favor.

 

305 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hornbeck v. Somerset County Bd. of Educ.


No. 93, September Term, 1981


Court of Appeals of Maryland


295 Md. 597; 458 A.2d 758; 1983 Md. LEXIS 222



April 5, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Ross, David, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree vacated; case remanded to the Circuit Court for Baltimore City for entry of a declaratory decree consistent with this opinion; costs to be paid by the plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, controller and school superintendent, challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland) that found that Maryland's system of financing public education violated Md. Const. art. VIII and art. 24 of the Md. Declaration of Rights because it permitted spending imbalances created by unequal tax revenues raised by local subdivisions.


OVERVIEW: Maryland funded its public education by creating an equalization formula for reducing the impact of wealth disparities among school districts. The formula contained a minimum per-student expenditure to support basic educational needs while permitting the counties to supplement the basic state-supported level with locally generated tax revenue. The circuit court ruled in favor of plaintiff Boards of Education by holding that this financing system violated Md. Const. art. VIII and Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 24, but on appeal by defendants, controller and school superintendent, the court reversed. It looked to the construction of Md. Const. art. VIII by reviewing the debates and proceedings in the constitutional conventions, concluding that the state constitution provided for a "thorough and efficient" system of education, not for a uniform system. The court used the rational basis standard of review to determine that the financing system did not violate either the state constitution or the declaration of rights. Maryland had a legitimate state interest in preserving local control over education, and the financing system was reasonably related to that interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's determination that Maryland's system for funding public education violated the state constitution and its declaration of rights because the constitution did not provide for a uniform system of education and the state's financing system was reasonably related to the legitimate state interest in preserving local control over education.

Insurance Comm'r of Maryland v. Blue Shield of Maryland, Inc.


No. 46, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


295 Md. 496; 456 A.2d 914; 1983 Md. LEXIS 215



March 4, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals from the Baltimore City Court; Grady, C. J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: In the appeal by the Insurance Commissioner: the appeal as to paragraph 2 of the order of December 31, 1981 is dismissed as moot; judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City as to paragraphs 3, 4 and 9 of said order is reversed; judgment as to paragraph 6 of said order is vacated and the appeal as to paragraph 6 is remanded to the Circuit Court for Baltimore City with instruction to dismiss the appeal as to that paragraph; as to paragraphs 5, 7 and 8 of the order, the judgment is affirmed. Costs to be paid 50% by the Insurance Commissioner, 25% by Blue Shield of Maryland, Inc. and 25% by Medical Service of the District of Columbia. In the appeal by Donald H. Dembo: judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City is affirmed. Costs to be paid by Donald H. Dembo.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance commissioner challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which found in favor of appellee plans and vacated the insurance commissioner's order relating to reimbursements as an excess of authority under Md. Code Ann., Ins. § 356. Appellant doctor challenged the dismissal of his complaint for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The insurance commissioner adopted an order regulating reimbursements by nonprofit health plans for services by providers other than hospitals. The plans challenged the order's validity. The lower court vacated the insurance commissioner's order, which was in excess of the insurance commissioner's authority under § 356. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part the lower court's judgment. Two paragraphs of the insurance commissioner's order were valid amendments of contracts with health care providers because they did not impair existing contract obligations or offend the Equal Protection clause. Two other paragraphs of the insurance commissioner's order, which changed the method of computer profiles, were invalid. The insurance commissioner did not have the visitorial power to compel the plans to change procedures that did not violate corporate by-laws or charters. Another paragraph was valid because the insurance commissioner had the authority to require the plans to submit their data. Finally, the doctor lacked standing to challenge the insurance commissioner's order because he was not a party to the administrative proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as to two paragraphs of the insurance commissioner's order. The court reversed the lower court's judgment as to three paragraphs of the insurance commissioner's order and affirmed as to three other paragraphs. The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the doctor's complaint.

Snowden v. Anne Arundel County


No. 92, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


295 Md. 429; 456 A.2d 380; 1983 Md. LEXIS 211



February 23, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Goudy, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee county in appellant's action challenging a county ordinance that created a criminal reimbursement expense fund for legal expenses incurred by certain county employees.


OVERVIEW: Anne Arundel County, Md., Code §§ 1-1400 through 1-1405 (1982), authorized the creation of a fund to prepay or reimburse legal expenses incurred by paid members of the county police and fire departments, detention center officers, and rescue squads charged with offenses arising from the performance of their duties. Appellant brought an action seeking a declaration that the ordinance violated the county charter and state law. The trial court rendered summary judgment for the county on the ground that that ordinance served a valid public purpose. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) the county was empowered to pass such ordinances as were deemed expedient in maintaining the peace, good government, health, and welfare of the county; (2) one limitation upon the county's broad grant of legislative power was Md. Const. Decl. Rights art. 15, which prohibited the expenditure of county tax revenues for other than a public purpose; and (3) the ordinance at issue served a public purpose because it better enabled the county to recruit and retain qualified public safety employees and to maintain morale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment rendered by the trial court in favor of the county in appellant's action challenging an ordinance that created a fund to prepay or reimburse certain legal expenses incurred by employees of the county police and fire departments.

 

308 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Taliaferro v. State


No. 101, September Term, 1981


Court of Appeals of Maryland


295 Md. 376; 456 A.2d 29; 1983 Md. LEXIS 208



February 10, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, McCullough, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed. Costs to be paid by the petitioner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought certiorari and a review of the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed defendant's convictions in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County for robbery with a deadly weapon and use of a handgun in the commission of a felony.


OVERVIEW: On the last day of his trial, defendant sought to introduce the testimony of an alibi witness whose identity was disclosed to the state for the first time on that date. The trial court excluded the alibi evidence for failure to comply with Md. R. Crim. P. 741. The court granted certiorari to consider whether the trial court's ruling constituted an abuse of discretion or a denial of due process. Defendant did not respond to the state's pre-trial request for disclosure of witnesses and certified prior to trial that all anticipated defense witnesses were identified. The court stressed the importance of a procedure that required notice of an alibi defense. A surprise alibi at trial would not allow state investigation of the facts. The court affirmed that the trial court was authorized to exclude the testimony of undisclosed witnesses as a discovery sanction, pursuant to Md. R. Crim. P. 741(g). The trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing the sanction. In the instant case, the violation of the rule was gross because there was no good faith attempt at compliance. There was no evidence showing that defendant was unaware of his alibi defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of special appeals, and defendant's convictions, holding that the trial court acted well within the bounds of its discretion in excluding defendant's alibi witness. Without any justifying excuse, defendant did not disclose an alibi witness until the close of the state's case in a jury trial.

 

309 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


In re James D.


No. 53, September Term, 1982


Court of Appeals of Maryland


295 Md. 314; 455 A.2d 966; 1983 Md. LEXIS 204



February 4, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Maryland, District 6, Montgomery County Juvenile Division; Moore, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; costs to be paid by Montgomery County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision of the District Court of Maryland, District 6, Montgomery County Juvenile Division, which ordered them to make restitution, as requested by appellee state pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-829 (1974, 1980 Repl. Vol., 1981 Cum. Supp.), for property damage caused by their son after he escaped from his court-ordered placement at a youth facility.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile escaped from his court-ordered placement at a youth facility and then broke into and set fire to a model home. Upon a petition by the state, the juvenile court subsequently ordered the juvenile's parents, pursuant to § 3-829, to make restitution in the amount of $ 5,000. On appeal, the court reversed. Specifically, the court held that the use of the term "parents" under § 3-829 could not apply to parents of a child in state custody. Moreover, the court ruled that to interpret § 3-829 more broadly so as to impose liability on parents of children who committed wrongful acts while in state custody would raise problems of constitutionality under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 24. Accordingly, the court concluded that the interpretation of "parent" in § 3-829 did not include the father or mother of a child where the child had been removed from their care and custody by court order and was not residing in their home at the time of the incident for which recovery was sought.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the juvenile court's order requiring the parents to make restitution for the property damages caused by the juvenile. In particular, the court held that the state law pertaining to restitution by parents could not be applied in a case where the child had been removed from the parents' care by court order and was not residing with the parents at the time of the incident for which recovery was sought.
