Attorney Gen. of Maryland v. Waldron


No. 45, September Term, 1980


Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 683; 426 A.2d 929; 1981 Md. LEXIS 198; 17 A.L.R.4th 794



March 13, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Bowen, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general, acting pursuant to the enforcement authority with regard to unauthorized practice vested in him by Md. Ann. Code, art. 10, § 26A, docketed an equity suit in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) seeking to enjoin respondent retired judge from the practice of law while receiving his pension and a declaration that art. 73B § 56(c) was constitutional. The circuit court denied relief.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court declared that § 56(c) was contrary to both the principle of separation of powers found in article 8 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights and the guaranties of equal protection of the law under both the federal and state constitutions. The court issued a writ of certiorari and agreed with the circuit court. Specifically, the court found that the defect contained in Md. Ann. Code art. 73B § 56(c) was that it, in effect, revoked the license of certain members of the bar based upon criteria entirely unrelated to their educational or moral fitness to engage in the practice of law. Therefore, the court held that § 56(c) was unrelated to the legislature's legitimate interest in prescribing proper prerequisites for entry into the profession. Accordingly, § 56(c) did not fall within an area of legitimate legislative concern regarding the legal profession and its practitioners and was unconstitutional. Additionally, the court determined that § 56(c) violated equal protection principles because the statutory discrimination against retired judges was not based on differences reasonably related to the legislative purpose of preventing impropriety.


OUTCOME: The decree of the circuit court denying the attorney general's request that sought to enjoin the judge from the practice of law following his retirement and a declaration that the controlling statute was constitutional was affirmed.

 

349 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Kindley v. Governor of Maryland


No. 155, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 620; 426 A.2d 908; 1981 Md. LEXIS 195



March 10, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Turk, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County affirmed; appellants to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) granted defendant state officials' motion for summary judgment in plaintiff taxpayers' action for declaratory and injunctive relief to prevent the state funding of abortions for indigents. The court granted the taxpayers' request for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that the payment of funds for abortions for indigents was illegal. The court held that the state medical program did not exclude the funding for an abortion which the woman and her physician determined to be in her best interest. The state program did not mention abortions or any other specific medical procedure but provided for a comprehensive program of medical care for indigent and medically indigent persons. The program was designed to permit indigent persons to receive the advantages of whatever health care was accepted as appropriate in the medical community. Compelling reasons, other than the risks of physical or mental illness, may have caused the woman and her physician to determine that abortion was appropriate. The statute reflected a broad legislative intent to ameliorate, as practicable, the consequences of inadequate or nonexistent medical care for the poor. The taxpayers' claim that the funds for the 1978 fiscal year were illegally expended for abortions was moot because that budget bill was no longer in effect and the taxpayers did not request an economic remedy for the funds already spent.


OUTCOME: The order of summary judgment in favor of the state officials was affirmed.

 

350 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Condore v. Prince George's County


No. 6, September Term, 1980


Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 516; 425 A.2d 1011; 1981 Md. LEXIS 187



February 19, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Blackwell, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; costs to be paid by Prince George's County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), held that appellant wife was liable to pay the hospital bill incurred by her deceased husband in appellee county hospital and granted summary judgment in favor of the county hospital on its claim for the unpaid amount. The wife appealed, and the state supreme court granted certiorari prior to review by the intermediate appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The county hospital filed suit against the wife to recover the unpaid amount of her deceased husband's hospital bill and filed a motion for summary judgment on its claim. The wife opposed the motion and asserted that she was not indebted to the county hospital because she had never agreed to be responsible for her husband's hospital bill. The trial court granted summary judgment in the county hospital's favor and held that, pursuant to Maryland's Equal Rights Amendment (ERA), art. 46 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights, the wife was liable for her husband's debt even though she had not contracted with the hospital to pay for the services rendered to her husband. The wife appealed, and the state supreme court granted certiorari prior to intermediate appellate review. The state supreme court held that, as a matter of law, the wife was not legally obligated to pay her husband's hospital bill. Rather than judicially expand the common law doctrine of necessaries by creating a new reciprocal liability upon the wife, pending legislative consideration of the matter, the court concluded that the necessaries doctrine, which violated the ERA, was no longer part of the Maryland common law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the county hospital.

Logan v. State


Nos. 24, 36, September Term, 1980


Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 460; 425 A.2d 632; 1981 Md. LEXIS 182



February 11, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Fisher, J., in No. 24 and Ross, J., in No. 36.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals in No. 24 affirmed. Costs to be paid by Theodore Russell Logan. Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals in No. 36 vacating the sentence imposed on Eugene Jerome Banks reversed, but in all other respects affirmed, and case remanded to that court with instructions to affirm the judgment embodying the conviction and sentence as entered by the Circuit Court for Prince George's County. Costs to be paid by Eugene Jerome Banks.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed separate judgments of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed one defendant's convictions for daytime housebreaking and petit larceny and affirmed the other defendant's convictions for second degree murder, false imprisonment, use of a handgun during the commission of a felony, armed robbery, and carrying a handgun. The appellate court vacated the murder defendant's sentence.


OVERVIEW: At the time each defendant was arrested, he was informed of his right to a prompt initial appearance before a commissioner pursuant to Md. Dist. R. 723a. Both defendants waived their right to an initial appearance and, as a result, statements they made to police after the waiver were used against them at trial. Defendants contended that the requirement of Md. Dist. R. 723 a could not be waived by a detained suspect. The court held that the prompt appearance requirement of Md. Dist. R. 723 a was susceptible of waiver by a suspect as long as the waiver was knowingly and intelligently made. The court found sufficient evidence that both defendants had knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently waived their rights to the initial appearance. Thus, the statements they made following the waiver were properly used against them at trial. The court reversed the appellate court's order vacating murder defendant's sentence because the issue underlying his sentencing had not been raised in either of the courts below. The court held that larceny defendant's sentence was proper because the trial court had not considered illegal confessions made by defendant to police.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and reversed and remanded the appellate court's judgment vacating murder defendant's sentence.

Prince George's County v. American Federation of State, etc.


No. 56, September Term, 1980


Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 388; 424 A.2d 770; 1981 Md. LEXIS 171



January 21, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed February 20, 1981; Denied March 2, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Levin, Jacob S., J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County affirmed. Appellant to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed the order from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which affirmed the order from the Public Employees Relations Board (PERB) that directed the county to formalize and execute a collective bargaining agreement that PERB found was agreed to by the county and defendant, union of municipal employees. The county's appeal was noted to the court of special appeals and certiorari was issued.


OVERVIEW: The county and the union began contract negotiations and reached a tentative agreement, which was signed by both parties but then rejected by the county executive. The union then filed an unfair labor practices charge with PERB against the county. The PERB hearing officer found numerous labor violations by the county and ordered it to execute and transmit to county council the tentative agreement. The circuit court found that there was substantial evidence to support the hearing officer's findings. On appeal, the court found that although there was no statutory provision conferring the county a right of appeal, it had jurisdiction to review a case or proceeding pending in the Court of Special Appeals in accordance with Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-201. The court then found that neither the hearing officer nor the circuit court exceeded their jurisdiction. PERB had jurisdiction to order that the tentative agreement be formalized and executed by the county under Labor Code § 114(c), Prince George's County, Md., 13A-114(c), which empowered an unfair labor practice panel to order an offending party to take such affirmative action as would effectuate the policies of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court, which directed the county to formalize and execute a collective bargaining agreement that PERB found was agreed to by the county and the union of municipal employees.

Stevenson v. State


No. 98, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 167; 423 A.2d 558; 1980 Md. LEXIS 245



December 17, 1980, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed defendant's convictions for first degree murder of her husband and for setting a fire while perpetrating a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that she was denied her Fourteenth Amendment right to due process when the trial court gave advisory rather than binding jury instructions and that Md. Const. Decl. On appeal, the court held that art. 23 did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment right to trial by jury as it applied to criminal trials under the Due Process Clause because the provision, making juries judges of the law, enhanced the purpose of a trial by jury by interposing a neutral interpreter of the law between the accused and the accusing government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

Fred W. Allnutt, Inc. v. Commissioner of Labor & Industry

Court of Appeals of Maryland


289 Md. 35; 421 A.2d 1360; 1980 Md. LEXIS 233



November 10, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Howard County; Wolff, J.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business petitioned for certiorari from the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which dismissed the business's appeal of a denial of a motion to quash an administrative search warrant issued by the district court under the Maryland Occupational Safety and Health Act (MOSHA), Md. 356 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Simms v. State


No. 110, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 712; 421 A.2d 957; 1980 Md. LEXIS 230



November 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Bothe, J., as to Simms and Thomas, J., as to Thomas.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Court of Special Appeals vacated, and cases remanded to that court with instructions to affirm the judgments of the Criminal Court of Baltimore except as to the sentences imposed, and to vacate the sentences and remand the cases for resentencing in accordance with this opinion. Costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a writ of certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed judgment of the trial court convicting defendants of simple assault and sentencing them to 12 years imprisonment. Defendants asserted that imposing a sentence for the lesser-included offense greater than the statutory maximum for the more serious crime violated their Eighth Amendment rights against cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with assault with intent to rob, and assault. Defendants were tried on both charges, with jeopardy attaching. Furthermore, in each proceeding, under the prosecution's evidence and theory of the case, the two charges were based upon the same acts. In each case, the assault with intent to rob charge was disposed of in each defendant's favor, and defendants were convicted of simple assault. Each defendant was sentenced to 12 years' imprisonment. Defendants sought review, asserting that it was error for the trial court to impose a sentence exceeding 10 years, the maximum sentence for an aggravated assault, for which they were acquitted. The appellate court affirmed judgment. On review by writ of certiorari, the court vacated the sentences and remanded the cases for resentencing because the 12 year sentences imposed on defendants were invalid. The court held that where the state charged both assault with intent to rob and simple assault, each charge being based on the same acts, and defendants were put in jeopardy, the state had in effect elected to prosecute for the 10 year maximum penalty specified for the greater offense of assault with intent to rob.


OUTCOME: The court vacated judgment and remanded the cases with instructions to affirm judgments of the trial court convicting defendants of simple assault, but ordered resentencing with a maximum penalty not to exceed the statutory 10 year imprisonment term for aggravated assault.

Board of Public Works v. Baltimore County


No. 58, September Term, 1980


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 678; 421 A.2d 588; 1980 Md. LEXIS 229



October 28, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; Sfekas, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County vacated and case remanded to that court for entry of a declaratory judgment in accordance with this opinion; costs to be equally divided between the parties; mandate shall issue forthwith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties, appellant state officials and appellee county, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which in an action by the county struck down as unconstitutional a provision in a statute, but held that the provision was severable so that the balance of the statute was enforceable. The court granted a writ of certiorari prior to a hearing by the Court of Special Appeals.


OVERVIEW: The challenged statute was a public law, which authorized the creation of a State debt for the design, planning, and construction of a performing arts center in the county. However, several amendments to the statute made the project contingent on the approval by a referendum of the legally qualified voters of the county. The Attorney General advised the Governor that he could not approve the bill for constitutionality. After the bill was signed by the Governor, the Board of Public Works refused to implement it on the advice of the Attorney General. The county filed the action for declaratory judgment. The trial court struck down so much of the challenged statute as required the approval of the voters, but held that the provision was severable so that the balance of the statute could be enforced. Both parties appealed. The court vacated the judgment and remanded for entry of a judgment that the invalidity of the statute was so fundamental that it was not susceptible of severability. The court held that a saving clause was not given effect where invalid provisions affected the dominant aim of the whole statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, and the case was remanded for a declaratory judgment that the entire statute was unconstitutional.

Apostol v. Anne Arundel County


No. 156, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 667; 421 A.2d 582; 1980 Md. LEXIS 227



October 27, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed November 20, 1980; Denied December 1, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Hopper and Goudy, JJ., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County vacated, and case remanded to that court with directions to dismiss the bill of complaint. Costs to be paid by the plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a petition and cross-petition for a writ of certiorari, plaintiff taxpayers appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which dismissed claims for injunctive relief, ordered tax refunds, and declared that the method used by defendants, county and county officials, to compute the property tax rate differential was proper as Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 32A(a) (1975 Repl. Vol., 1979 Cum. Supp.) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 32A(a) (1975 Repl. Vol., 1979 Cum. Supp.) authorized a county to tax property, located within a municipal corporation in the county, at less than the general county property tax rate if the municipality performed government services or programs. Md. Ann. Code art. 81, § 12G-8 prohibited two counties from imposing taxes upon residents of any incorporated municipality for services that the municipality provided for its residents. As a result of the ongoing tax dispute between the residents of the county and the remainder of the county over the tax rate differential, the taxpayers filed this class action. The court vacated the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for dismissal of the declaratory action. Since the taxpayers paid the disputed property taxes, no issue concerning any possible legislative intent to supplant an existing common law or declaratory judgment remedy could lie. The only remedy that existed was the statutory authorization for a refund that was expressly provided by the statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 81, §§ 214, 214C, 229. The payment of the taxes during the pendency of the court action terminated the taxpayers' right to continue.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to dismiss the taxpayer's declaratory judgment action. The court ordered the taxpayers to pay the costs.

 

359 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Department of Public Safety & Correctional Services v. Le Van


No. 5, September Term, 1980


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 533; 419 A.2d 1052; 1980 Md. LEXIS 217



September 15, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Williams, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed and case remanded to that court for the passage of an order affirming in part and reversing in part the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County with directions for further remand by it to the Sundry Claims Board for further proceedings consistent with this opinion; appellee to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Public Safety and Correctional Services challenged an order from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) that dismissed its appeal after finding that a trial court's remand to the Sundry Claims Board of an appeal from that board was not an appealable final order in appellee inmate's claim for disability benefits under Md. Ann. Code art. 41 (Act), §188A (1957, 1978 Repl. Vol.).


OVERVIEW: The inmate sustained an injury while employed as a janitor at a prison, and the board awarded compensation under the Act. Dissatisfied, the inmate appealed to the trial court, which affirmed the board's finding of a partial permanent disability but remanded to the board for explicit findings on the degree of disability and on earnings in accordance with the Workmen's Compensation statute. The department sought review of this order in the intermediate appellate court, which dismissed the appeal after concluding that there had been no final judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal, holding that the trial court's order was an appealable final judgment that settled the rights of the parties under Md. Ann. Code art. 41, § 188A(h). The court also found that although the trial court correctly remanded the case to the board for a determination of the inmate's disability, there was no basis for the trial court's conclusion that the compensation was to be calculated under the Workmen's Compensation statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the intermediate appellate court's order that dismissed the department's appeal of trial court's remand of a disability benefits decision to the board. The case was remanded to the intermediate appellate court for passage of an order affirming the trial court's finding of disability but reversing its order to calculate benefits based on the Workmen's Compensation statute.

 

360 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


McClain v. State


No. 94, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 456; 419 A.2d 369; 1980 Md. LEXIS 211



September 9, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Howard, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; case remanded to the Court of Special Appeals for passage of an order reversing the judgment of the Criminal Court of Baltimore and further remanding the case for a new trial; costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of certiorari from the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which, pursuant to a jury verdict, convicted defendant of murder in the first degree. Certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threw a baby down the trash chute of a building. Defendant gave an inculpatory statement the day after his arrest. On review, the questions before the court were: (1) whether defendant preserved for appellate review the issue of whether statements obtained from him in violation of former Md. Dist. R. 709(a) were inadmissible, as the court had held in a subsequent case; and if so (2) whether the court's decision in that subsequent case was applicable to defendant's case, which was tried before the decision in the subsequent case, but reached appellate review after that decision. The court concluded that the issue of the state's violation of former Md. Dist. R. 723(a) was not properly before it. The court reversed the affirmance of the conviction, because defendant's argument for suppression, though directed at voluntariness, included that the statements were obtained in violation of former Md. Dist. R. 709(a). Also, the court's prior applications of the Linkletter formula had never led it to refuse to apply a new rule to a case on direct review in which the issue of the new rule was raised, which was pending at the time of the formulation of the new rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court that affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of murder. The case was remanded to the appellate court for passage of an order reversing the trial court's judgment and further remanding the case for a new trial.

Di Grazia v. County Executive for Montgomery County


No. 123, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 437; 418 A.2d 1191; 1980 Md. LEXIS 213; 115 L.R.R.M. 4409



September 8, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed October 8, 1980; Denied October 10, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Fairbanks, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; case remanded to the Court of Special Appeals for remand to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County with directions that the summary judgment be vacated and further proceedings conducted consistent with this opinion; costs to abide the result.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, public employee, sought review through a writ of certiorari of the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant, County Executive for Montgomery County, against plaintiff's complaint that he had been removed from his office in violation of the Law Enforcement Officers' Bill of Rights, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 727-734D.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, public employee, challenged the lower court's decision to affirm the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant, County Executive for Montgomery County, and claimed that he was improperly removed by defendant from his position in violation of the Law Enforcement Officers' Bill of Rights, (LEOBR) Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 727-734D. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the lower court for remand to the trial court with directions to vacate summary judgment and for further proceedings, as there were genuine issues of material fact. Summary judgment was improperly based on inapplicability of LEOBR, as Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 728(13) specifically contemplated protection for the heads of police departments. Subsequently, whether plaintiff had been removed from office in violation of protections afforded under LEOBR for the lawful exercise of his constitutional freedom of speech rights was a mixed question of law and fact, not appropriate for resolution by summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment against plaintiff public employee's complaint of improper removal from office, as there were genuine issues of material fact, such a determination involved mixed questions of law and fact, and it was therefore inappropriately resolved by summary judgment.

Prince George's County v. Blumberg


No. 147, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 275; 418 A.2d 1155; 1980 Md. LEXIS 205



August 22, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed September 19, 1980; Denied September 26, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Bowen, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals as it pertains to Prince George's County and the Washington Suburban Sanitary Commission reversed and case remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment entered in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County against those two defendants without a new trial. Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals as to William W. Gullett and Winfield M. Kelley, Jr., affirmed. Costs to be paid by Marvin and Herschel Blumberg.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a county and a sanitary commission, appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the trial court's order directing the sanitary commission to reissue respondent developers' revoked building and water-sewer permits and awarding the developers compensatory damages against the county.


OVERVIEW: The developers planned to construct a high-rise building on their land that situated in an area of restricted sewer service. After obtaining water-sewer and building permits from the sanitary commission and the county respectively, the developers began construction. When both permits were revoked, the developers filed a complaint against the county and sanitary commission, seeking injunctive and declaratory relief. On appeal, the court concluded that the lower court's judgment for the developers was improper as the developers failed to exhaust the available administrative remedies. Under Prince George's County, Md., Code § 4-140, the developers could have sought review of the revocation of the permits or the building official's refusal to reinstate the building permit before the county's board of appeals established pursuant to the Express Powers Act, codified at Md. Ann. Code art. 25A, § 5 (1957).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order and remanded the case to the lower court with instructions to reverse the judgment entered by the trial court against the sanitary commission and the county.

State v. Denten Corp.


No. 112, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


288 Md. 178; 416 A.2d 271; 1980 Md. LEXIS 197



July 9, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Criminal Court of Baltimore; Hammerman, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court of Baltimore reversed and cases remanded for further proceedings. Costs to be paid by the appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for a writ of certiorari seeking a review of an order of the Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland), which granted defendants' motions to dismiss, filed pursuant to Md. R. 736, the documents charging them with a violation of the requirement of Md. Ann. Code art. 66A, § 19(b) (1957) that a film be licensed prior to its showing. Defendants asserted that § 19(b) was unconstitutionally applied.


OVERVIEW: Maryland's motion picture censorship law required that a license to show a film first have been obtained prior to its showing. The police executed a search warrant and seized the only copies of several films owned by defendants for which they had not obtained a license from the Maryland State Board of Censors. Defendants were convicted of violating § 19(b) and they appealed their convictions. Before the appeal was heard, the seized films were destroyed by the State. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the charges on the ground that § 19(b) was being unconstitutionally applied. Under the law applicable to allegedly obscene films, material seized on the basis of obscenity had to have been copied and returned to an offender until an adjudication that the material was obscene. Defendants asserted that because their materials were not returned to them, dismissal was appropriate. The court held that the issues were distinct because the obscene materials were presumptively protected while the unlicensed materials were not. Defendants had no right to exhibit an unlicensed film and the protections afforded the allegedly obscene materials did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the criminal court's order dismissing the charging documents and remanded the cases for further proceedings.

Tichnell v. State


Nos. 73, 104, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


287 Md. 695; 415 A.2d 830; 1980 Md. LEXIS 187



June 10, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of Sentence of Death and Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County; Pollitt, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed, except as to the imposition of the death sentence; death sentence vacated and case remanded to the Circuit Court for Wicomico County for a new sentencing proceeding under § 413 of Art. 27; each party to pay own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death for shooting a police officer after breaking into a store and stealing guns.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another broke into a store, stole guns, and were accosted by a deputy sheriff, who was then killed by defendant. Defendant claimed that the shooting was in self-defense. The trial court convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but vacated the death sentence. The court held that there was no error in the joinder of the indictments for murder and robbery because they were based on the same act or transaction. There was no denial of defendant's right under Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 20 to be tried where the facts of the case arose in changing venue. He was not denied a fair trial due to any hostile atmosphere. There was no plain error in the jury instructions. The jury could rationally find defendant guilty of first-degree murder despite his claim of self-defense. Maryland's death penalty statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 412-414, was not facially unconstitutional. The case was remanded for another sentencing hearing due to the trial judge saying, before the completion of evidence in the case, that he was not sure that it was a death penalty case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the death sentence and remanded. The court held that defendant was entitled to a fresh sentencing hearing due to the trial judge's remark during trial regarding the death penalty. There was no error in joinder of the indictments, no denial of a fair trial due to hostile atmosphere, no plain error in jury instructions, and the death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.

Cheeks v. Cedlair Corp.


No. 114, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


287 Md. 595; 415 A.2d 255; 1980 Md. LEXIS 179



June 3, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Kaplan, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City (Maryland), which determined that a proposed referendum purportedly authorized by MD. Const. art. XI-A to create a new article to the charter by establishing a comprehensive system of rent control and a new city agency to be known as the Tenant-Landlord Commission, was in error.


OVERVIEW: The proposed charter amendment was initiated by a number of individuals and organizations (citizens), who were dissatisfied with the refusal of the Baltimore City Council to enact continuing rent control legislation. Purporting to act under MD. Const. § 5 of art. XI-A, the citizens completed a petition to submit the amendment to a vote of the city electorate. However, the appellees, city counsel, and other officials, were opposed to the referendum, contending that the amendment divested the city council of its constitutionally vested legislative powers in violation of the provisions of MD. Const. amend. § 3 art. XI-A. The court agreed with the opponents of the referendum, and it adopted their arguments. The court said that the charter amendment proposed was intended not simply to create a new city agency, but rather to establish a comprehensive system for regulating rents within the city's residential housing market. That was a clear indication that the amendment was essentially legislative in character, and therefore it was prohibited under the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the proposed referendum was invalid because it exceeded the scope allowing such proposals because it was legislative in nature. The court also assessed costs to the citizens.

Cider Barrel Mobile Home Court v. Eader


No. 86, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


287 Md. 571; 414 A.2d 1246; 1980 Md. LEXIS 173



May 26, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Mathias, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, park and its owner, petitioned for a writ of certiorari concerning an order from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which in appellee park residents' challenge to park rules, declared constitutional the Mobile Home Park Act (Act), Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. §§ 8A-101 - 114 (1979, 1979 Cum. Supp.) and found that appellants were in violation of such Act.


OVERVIEW: The park residents filed a suit against appellants challenging a rule which required that all homes retained after resale in the park had to meet minimum standards with respect to size, quality, and construction. The park residents claimed that they were either unable to sell their homes or were forced to sell them at reduced prices. The lower court declared that the rule violated the Act, which under Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 8A-110(b) prohibited park owners from preventing the sale of a home or requiring its removal due to a sale. Appellants petitioned for a writ of certiorari alleging that the Act was an unconstitutional taking of property. The court granted the writ and affirmed the judgment. The court found that appellants had not been permanently deprived of their right to use of the land for the purposes other than a mobile home park because the Act did not prevent appellants from terminating a tenancy by means other than eviction to discontinue park operations. The court also determined that notwithstanding the Act's restrictions, appellants continued the operation of the park without a decrease in occupancy, loss of revenue, or interference with marketability.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellants' writ of certiorari and affirmed a judgment declaring that appellants' rule requiring the removal of the park residents' homes after resale, if they failed to meet minimum established standards, violated federal statutory law prohibiting such removal and that such law was constitutional.

Stevenson v. State


No. 82, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


287 Md. 504; 413 A.2d 1340; 1980 Md. LEXIS 169



May 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Melbourne, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed. Costs to be paid by the petitioners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed defendants' convictions of two counts of robbery with a deadly weapon and one count of using a handgun in the commission of a crime of violence.


OVERVIEW: After defendants were convicted of two counts of robbery with a deadly weapon and one count of using a handgun in the commission of a crime of violence, defendants appealed. Defendants argued that an extraterritorial arrest by a police officer was not that of a private citizen if the officer was acting under color of his office at the time of the arrest. The court affirmed, holding that the Washington officers did not see the cloud of red smoke, paper flying out of the bag, or the flight of defendants from the bank because of their status as officers, but merely observed what every private citizen, close enough to do, could have perceived. The court held that the police officers were functioning in a private rather than official capacity for the purpose of evaluating the legality of the arrests and that the facts, taken together, supported the finding that the officers acted with probable cause. The court further held that as private citizens, the officers had reasonable grounds to believe not only that a felony had occurred, but also that defendants had committed it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of robbery with a deadly weapon and use of a handgun in the commission of a violent crime. The court held that citizen arrests remained viable in Maryland and that as private citizens, the Washington officers had reasonable grounds to believe not only that a felony had occurred, but also that defendants had committed it.

Montgomery County Bd. of Realtors, Inc. v. Montgomery County


No. 85, September Term, 1979.


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


287 Md. 101; 411 A.2d 97; 1980 Md. LEXIS 247



February 11, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration filed March 12, 1980; denied March 21, 1980. 


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County.

(MATIAS, J.), pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.

Bill of complaint by Montgomery County Board of Realtors, Inc., John C. Walker Realty Corp. and Ed Ward W. Schultz against Montgomery County, Maryland, seeking to declare invalid the Montgomery County "Real Property Tax Recapture" Statute. Montgomery County Code (1972, 1977 Repl. Vol.) § 52-16C. From a decree upholding the validity of the Statute, the plaintiffs appealed to the Court of Special Appeals. Certiorari was granted prior to hearing in that court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; appellee to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county board of realtors and two realtors, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which upheld the validity of appellee county's "Real Property Tax Recapture" against their challenge.


OVERVIEW: The county council enacted the recapture statute to attempt to recover for the county real property taxes that should have been paid but were not because of low assessments. The trial court called it a windfall profits tax. The county called it an excise tax. The tax was levied when real estate was transferred upon the difference between the sale price and the assessed vale of the property. The court said it was a tax upon real property and in conflict with the state's comprehensive legislative scheme for the taxation of real property contained in Md. Code art. 81. Under Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 3, in case of any conflict between a local law and any Public General Law, the Public General Law controlled. The county was not without remedies. Article 81 provided a method for the county to challenge real property assessments if it believed that the property was undervalued. The court held as an additional ground for invalidating the statute that the state had preempted the field of real property taxation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Washington Nat'l Arena Ltd. Partnership v. Treasurer, Prince George's County


No. 124, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


287 Md. 38; 410 A.2d 1060; 1980 Md. LEXIS 138



February 7, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Meloy, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County reversed, and case remanded to that court for the entry of an order consistent with this opinion. Respondent to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which affirmed a finding that a recordation tax rate imposed by respondent county treasurer was a curative act and could be retroactively applied without impairing their constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought partial refunds for overpayment of recordation taxes. Their timely claims were disallowed by operation of law because of the county's failure to act within six months. A state tax court upheld the tax, finding that, chapter 129 of the Acts of 1976, enacted while the case was pending, was "a curative act" which resurrected a prior county resolution fixing the recordation tax rate at $ 1.65 per $ 500. The circuit court affirmed. On writ of certiorari to the court of appeals, the court reversed and remanded, holding that chapter 129 of the Acts of 1976 did not rectify a "technical" defect in county authority to collect recordation taxes at the $ 1.65 rate. The court found that prior to ch. 129 and in effect at the time the taxpayers' taxable transactions were completed as well as when they filed claims for refunds, the maximum county recordation tax rate was $ 1.10. The court concluded that the retroactive application of ch. 129 of the Acts of 1976 to the taxpayers' recording transactions would impair property rights in violation of the United States Constitution and the Maryland Declaration of Rights. Thus, the taxpayers were entitled to refunds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgement in favor of the county treasurer.

Pitsenberger v. Pitsenberger


No. 80, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


287 Md. 20; 410 A.2d 1052; 1980 Md. LEXIS 132



January 31, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Mathias, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) awarding appellee wife pendente lite custody of their minor children, child support, and exclusive use of the family home, on the grounds that Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-6A-06 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee wife left the family home with her minor children and filed for divorce. Appellee was awarded pendente lite custody of the children, child support, and, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-6A-06, exclusive use of the family home. Appellant husband contended that § 3-6A-06 violated procedural due process by authorizing a pendente lite use and possession award of the family home without a preliminary showing by appellee that grounds existed for a divorce. Appellant also claimed that § 3-6A-06 permitted the unlawful taking of private property without just compensation in violation of the federal and state constitutions. The circuit court ruled against appellant and the court granted certiorari. The court affirmed, holding that the validity of the divorce was to be ultimately determined at a subsequent hearing and that the interests of the state in protecting the welfare of the children required a pendente lite possession award without a full hearing on the merits of the divorce. The court also held that § 3-6A-06 was constitutional because appellant was not deprived of all beneficial use of his property because it was being used to house his children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that appellant husband's procedural due process rights were not violated by the pendente lite award of exclusive use of the family home to appellee wife and their minor children without a preliminary hearing on the merits of the divorce because of the state's important interest in protecting the children's welfare.

Du Bois v. College Park


No. 139, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


286 Md. 677; 410 A.2d 577; 1980 Md. LEXIS 126



January 28, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Mattingly, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded to the Circuit Court for Prince George's County for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Appellees to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff college students sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) approving defendant city's revised apportionment plan for council districts. The students had alleged that the council districts were unequally apportioned.


OVERVIEW: The students filed a class action against the city, alleging that the 1970 census showed that the council districts were unequally apportioned. The students claimed that as a result of the malapportionment, their votes were unconstitutionally diluted. The trial court ordered the city to adopt a revised apportionment plan. A final judgment approving the new plan was entered. The students filed an appeal, contending that the revised plan excluded from its population apportionment base a large segment of students who lived in the college dormitories. The court reversed and remanded the order approving the plan. The court found that the city offered no explanation for treating significant groups of students differently. The court further found that permitting a large number of students who had not registered to vote to be included within the apportionment base while excluding others who were similarly situated did not insure that only true domicilaries would be counted. Accordingly, the court held that the plan contained classifications that could not be justified when carefully and meticulously scrutinized. The plan violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The order approving the city's revised apportionment plan for council districts was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Supermarkets General Corp. v. State


Nos. 63, 72, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


286 Md. 611; 409 A.2d 250; 1979 Md. LEXIS 323



December 24, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 63 (Supermarkets Gen.) Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Hopper, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Scott's Corp. and Stewart & Co.) Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Baltimore County; DeWaters, J.

No. 72 (Toys "R" Us, Inc.) Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Hopper, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; costs to be paid by appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant retailers were convicted of violating Maryland's Sunday closing laws in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County and the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland). They appealed and argued that the Sunday closing laws were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the exceptions of various commodities, businesses and persons from the Sunday prohibitions were without rational and substantial relation to the object of the legislation and, therefore, were arbitrary, oppressive and unreasonable. The court held that: (1) the Sunday closing laws did not involve a fundamental right nor did they operate to the peculiar disadvantage of a suspect class; (2) the exemption of the specified establishments, businesses, and classes of persons were necessary in the counties concerned, either for the health of the populace or for the enhancement of the recreational atmosphere of the day; (3) there was no invidious discrimination and the purpose of providing a day on which there was a lesser degree of business activity was a valid reason for Sunday closing laws; (4) the Sunday closing laws in Maryland did not constitute the establishment of religion in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I and Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 36; and (5) a monopoly within the contemplation of Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 41 was not suffered by the law under which defendants were convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial courts' judgments, holding that the Sunday closing laws were constitutionally valid.

Watson v. State


No. 34, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


286 Md. 291; 407 A.2d 324; 1979 Md. LEXIS 290



November 6, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Arabian, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed and case remanded to that court with instructions to vacate the sentence which was imposed by the Criminal Court of Baltimore and then remand the case to that court with direction that it impose a new sentence arrived at in conformity with this opinion. Pursuant to Md. Rule 882f, costs are not reallocated as part of the judgment of this Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of rape in the second degree by the Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland) and sentenced to 20 years imprisonment. The court granted defendant's petition for the issuance of a writ of certiorari. The question presented was whether the sentence imposed constituted cruel and unusual punishment or was otherwise improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 21 years old, engaged in vaginal intercourse with a 13-year-old girl. The girl had freely and voluntarily engaged in the sexual activity. To aid in the imposition of punishment, the trial court requested a pre-sentence medical report and a pre-sentence probation report at the conclusion of the guilt phase of the trial. The medical report recommended a maximum sentence of incarceration and confinement at a particular institution. The trial court stated that it could only send defendant there if defendant wished it. Defendant did not so the trial court imposed the maximum punishment. The court found that this belief of the trial court, and its subsequent action apparently predicated upon that belief, required that the sentence imposed be vacated and that the case be remanded for resentencing. Md. Ann. Code art. 31B did not require defendant's consent to a referral to the institution. Although the sentence imposed by the trial court did not exceed the maximum allowed, the trial court's determination was based upon an impermissible consideration because of its mistaken belief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with instructions to vacate the sentence and then remand the case to the trial court with direction that it impose a new sentence arrived at in conformity with its opinion.

 

376 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Maryland-National Capital Park & Planning Com. v. Chadwick


No. 2, September Term, 1979


Court of Appeals of Maryland


286 Md. 1; 405 A.2d 241; 1979 Md. LEXIS 324



September 11, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; McAuliffe, John F., J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant planning commission sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which found that the planning commission unconstitutionally deprived the landowners of the use of their property without just compensation by placing appellee landowners' property in public "reservation" without their consent for a period not to exceed three years as authorized by Montgomery County, Md., Code § 50-31(a).


OVERVIEW: The planning commission determined that the landowners' property was within a planned park and lake expansion and that a planned dam site would flood a road providing access to the landowners' proposed subdivision. The court found that the planning commission's resolution placing the landowners' property in reservation for a period up to three years stripped them of all reasonable use of their property and was tantamount to a "taking" without compensation. The court construed § 50-31 as not permitting the landowners to make, as a matter of right, any beneficial use of the property placed in reservation other than to remove trash and weeds. The court determined that restrictions of such totality came within the principle that a governmental restriction imposed on the use of land may be so onerous as to constitute a taking which constitutionally requires the payment of just compensation. Because the planning commission's resolution did not provide for compensation, the court concluded that it was unconstitutional and of no effect. Consequently, the trial court properly required the planning commission to approve the landowners' preliminary subdivision plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment requiring the planning commission to forthwith approve the landowners' preliminary subdivision plan.

 

377 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


In re Laurence T.


No. 92, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 621; 403 A.2d 1256; 1979 Md. LEXIS 258



July 26, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. District Court of Maryland for Montgomery County sitting as a Juvenile Court, Moore, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded to that court to enter an order affirming the judgment of the District Court; Montgomery County to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, appealed from a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed a decision of the trial court dismissing a delinquency petition against appellant as violative of due process and equal protection principles. The petition had been filed against appellant but not his confederates, whose parent had promised to pay restitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and two other juveniles allegedly broke into a private residence, ransacked the house, and caused $ 1,200 in damage. The three boys were apprehended at the scene and taken into custody. The father of appellant's two confederates took charge of his sons shortly thereafter and promised to pay for two-thirds of the damage. Appellant's mother, however, refused to take immediate custody of her son and made no firm commitment to make restitution. The court held that appellant had met his burden of proving discriminatory enforcement of the laws in violation of the Equal Protection Clause. The court failed to discern any rational relation between the purpose of juvenile proceedings, to afford treatment and rehabilitation to the offender, and the criterion the State admittedly used as a basis for its differentiation between appellant and the other boys, whether a juvenile's parent promised to make restitution. Moreover, the State's action against appellant was the product of a deliberative process. The Equal Protection Clause prohibited state law enforcement officials from purposefully and intentionally singling out individuals for disparate treatment on a discriminatory basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of special appeals and remanded the case to that court to enter an order affirming the judgment of the district court.

In re Leroy T.


No. 81, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 508; 403 A.2d 1226; 1979 Md. LEXIS 256



July 23, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City, Division for Juvenile Causes; Hargrove, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City, Division for Juvenile Causes (Maryland), which adjudicated him delinquent on charges of being in possession of a criminal tool, namely, pliers, in violation of Baltimore, Md., City Code art. 19, § 9(a)(5) (1976). Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 9(a)(5) under Md. Const. art. 24 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant, who was a 13 years old, unsuccessfully attempt to open the door of a car parked in a parking lot. Defendant then approached a second car, placed a key in its lock, removed a pair of pliers from his pocket and, without success, attempted to turn the key. When defendant noticed the officer, he dropped both the pliers and the key and began to walk away. Defendant was arrested and charged with and convicted of being delinquent in that he unlawfully did possess pliers with the purpose of committing an unlawful act. Before the appellate court addressed defendant's appeal, the court granted defendant certiorari. The court ruled that Baltimore, Md., City Code art. § 9(a)(5) was unconstitutionally vague, in violation of Md. Const. art. 24 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Specifically, the court ruled that the ordinance's provision that prohibited possession of tools "commonly used for criminal use" failed to afford fair notice of the prohibited devices and failed to provide adequate guidelines for enforcement. That provision of the ordinance was severed from the remainder of the ordinance, which was not unconstitutionally vague in describing prohibited tools.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

379 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. Thompson


No. 85, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 488; 404 A.2d 269; 1979 Md. LEXIS 243



July 20, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Childs, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; petitioner to pay the costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner minor child, on certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland). The child asked that the court strike down as unconstitutional the portion of Md. Code art. 16, § 66(e) (1957, 1973 Repl. Vol.), which required any action to establish an individual as the father of an illegitimate child to be commenced within two years after the birth of such child.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother brought a paternity action against the alleged father slightly two years after the child's birth. The matter was dormant for several years until a prosecutor requested that summons be issued. The alleged father claimed the action was time barred and the trial court dismissed it. The child was not ever made a party. The court affirmed, finding that illegitimacy was not a favored status and did not require strict scrutiny. The statute of limitations was proper because after a number of years from contact with the mother an alleged father could have substantial difficulty in establishing that he was not the only individual who could have sired the child. The court found that the statute affected no fundamental right of the child because she could still get support from the mother or public funds. For the court to take cognizance of scientific blood testing techniques it would have been incumbent upon the child to adduce evidence showing that this technique was sufficiently established to have gained general acceptance in its particular field.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

380 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Washabaugh v. Washabaugh


Nos. 89, 90, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 393; 404 A.2d 1027; 1979 Md. LEXIS 247



July 13, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (sitting in banc), pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Order dismissing the appeal in No. 89 vacated and case remanded to the court in banc for consideration of points properly reserved. Costs to abide the final result. Order dismissing the appeal in No. 90 vacated and case remanded to the court in banc for consideration of points properly reserved. Costs to abide the final result.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate actions, petitioners, who were both non-residents of Baltimore City, sought review of decisions by the Seventh Judicial Circuit (Maryland), which dismissed petitioners' appeals to the in banc court on the grounds that Md. Const. art. IV, § 22, which allowed appeals to an in banc court, was violative of the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: In two cases, petitioners appealed adverse judgments to in banc courts pursuant to § 22. The in banc courts, however, held that § 22 violated the equal protection clause, and they dismissed petitioners' appeals. On review, the court vacated the orders of dismissal. The court held that it was authorized to review the in banc courts' decisions that in banc courts should not exist. The court then applied the rational basis test and found that, even assuming that § 22 did not allow residents of Baltimore City an in banc appeal, § 22 did not violate the equal protection clause. The court noted that there was no per se constitutional limitation upon intrastate differences in judicial organization and procedures. The statistics did not establish the litigational burden upon the Baltimore City courts, and the one-year statistics concerning the caseloads of the in banc courts did not warrant overturning a century-old constitutional provision. Moreover, the proliferation of courts and judges in Baltimore City would cause difficulty and inconvenience in coordinating in banc appeals there. The court instructed that, on remand, the in banc courts should consist of only three members.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the in banc courts' orders dismissing petitioners' appeals. The court remanded the actions to the in banc courts to consider the appeals.

Chairman of Board of Trustees v. Waldron


No. 40, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 175; 401 A.2d 172; 1979 Md. LEXIS 210



May 10, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Calvert County; Bowen, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court for Calvert County vacated and case remanded with direction that it dismiss the proceedings. Costs to be paid equally by the parties.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the chairman and the board of trustees of the state employees' retirement system (board), petitioned for a writ of certiorari to review the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which declared Md. Ann. Code 73B, § 56(c) to be unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, thus permitting respondent retired judge both to receive his pension and practice law in Maryland.


OVERVIEW: Section 56(c) barred any retired judge who accepted a pension from practicing law. Preliminarily, the court recognized the delicacy of its deciding a case in which the members of the court had an indirect interest, but it declared that under the circumstances, the disqualification of all the judges would destroy the only tribunal in which relief could be sought. The rule as to the disqualification had to yield to the right of appeal. The court then held that dismissal of the retired judge's declaratory judgment action was required, because the judge failed to join any party necessary to litigate the issue, in that none of the petitioners could claim any interest that would be affected by the declaration. While § 56(c) prohibited a retired judge who accepted a pension from engaging in the practice of law for compensation, it did not give the board the power to enforce that prohibition. Because none of the necessary parties who had the power to initiate an action against one engaged in the unauthorized practice of law were joined as a defendant, the court dismissed the case without deciding the question of whether § 56(c) violated the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was vacated and the case was remanded with direction that it dismiss the proceedings.

In re Oldtowne Legal Clinic, P.A.


Misc. No. 11, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 132; 400 A.2d 1111; 1979 Md. LEXIS 216



May 7, 1979, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner law firm sought a certificate of authorization of corporation name as a separate professional association under the Professional Service Corporation Act, Md. Corporations and Associations Code Ann. §§ 5-101 through 5-122. Respondent bar association asserted that Md. Lawyer's R. Prof. Conduct 2-102(A) prohibited lawyers from practicing law under a trade name.


OVERVIEW: The law firm argued that a trade name was commercial speech entitled to the same protection afforded other forms of speech, and so, as long as its was not deceptive, the restriction of Md. Lawyer's R. Prof. Conduct 2-102(A) violated U.S. Const. amend. I and Article 40 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights. The court rejected that argument and denied the petition for a certificate authorizing the use of a trade name under which the law firm was to have practiced law. The court observed that historically the use of trade names had been prohibited, and concluded the proposed trade name of the law firm conflicted with the rule 2-102(A), in violation of the Professional Services Act, Md. Corporations and Associations Code Ann. § 5-110(2), and so was not approved. The court reasoned further that the restriction on potentially deceptive and misleading commercial speech did not violate either the First Amendment or Article 40 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights. Furthermore, the court held that the equal protection of the law was not violated by the different treatment between lawyers and physicians' use of trade names because different ethical considerations were at issue.


OUTCOME: The court denied the law firm its request for a certificate of authorization for a corporate name that it was to have used to practice law under an assumed trade name because although a form of commercial speech, it was subject to state restriction, which neither violated the First Amendment, the Maryland Declaration of Rights, nor the equal protection clause.

Davis v. State


No. 100, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 19; 400 A.2d 406; 1979 Md. LEXIS 199



April 23, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Greenfeld, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals affirmed in part and vacated in part and case remanded to that court with direction to remand to the Criminal Court of Baltimore for further proceedings, all in accordance with this opinion. Costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court of Baltimore (Maryland) of two armed robberies, two assaults, and carrying of a concealed weapon. Following denial of his direct appeal, defendant appealed under the Uniform Post Conviction Procedure Act, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 645A-645J. The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari to consider whether the instruction to the jury regarding alibi required reversal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury that "in order to prove an alibi conclusively, the testimony must cover the whole time in which the crime by any possibility might have been committed and it should be rigid, it should be subjected to rigid scrutiny." The court held that the jury instruction was erroneous because it improperly shifted the burden of proof to defendant. However, the hearing judge did not err in denying defendant's post conviction relief under Md. Ann. Code, art. 27, § 645A(d), because that provision was only triggered when a new standard was imposed on the trial courts, and no new standard was imposed regarding jury instructions. The court also held that there was no impediment to finding that the erroneous instruction was waived, and a new trial was not required under Md. Ann. Code, art. 27, § 645A(c). However, because the post conviction judge failed to rule on the issue of whether defense counsel was ineffective for failing to object to the erroneous instruction, and made no findings of fact thereon, the court remanded to the post conviction court for further inquiry and factual findings on that issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment to the extent that it denied defendant's appeal for violations of the Uniform Post Conviction Procedure Act. The court vacated the judgment with respect to the issue concerning effective assistance of counsel and remanded with directions for further inquiry, factual findings, and a ruling with respect to that issue.

Unnamed Physician v. Commission on Medical Discipline


No. 33, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


285 Md. 1; 400 A.2d 396; 1979 Md. LEXIS 200



April 23, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Baltimore County, MacDaniel, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed in part and affirmed in part; case remanded to that court for proceedings consistent with this opinion; appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that, except for any minutes or notes, the records of a hospital's medical review committee could be subpoenaed by appellee Commission on Medical Discipline of Maryland because a disciplinary proceeding before appellee was not a civil action within the meaning of Md. Ann. Code art. 43, § 134A(d) (1957, 1971 Repl. Vol., 1978 Supp.)


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an investigation into the medical malpractice of appellant physician, appellee Commission on Medical Discipline of Maryland filed a petition to enforce subpoenas requiring members of a hospital's executive committee to produce the records of a medical review committee that were pertinent to the privileges and practice of appellant. The appellate court determined that Md. Ann. Code art. 43, § 134A(d) (1957, 1971 Repl. Vol., 1978 Supp.), did not protect the subpoenaed materials from discovery because a proceeding before appellee was not a civil action within the meaning of § 134A(d), but that Md. Ann. Code art. 43, § 130A(a)(3) precluded the discovery of any of the medical review committee's "minutes or notes." On appeal, the court held that all of the subpoenaed materials, including the committee's "minutes and notes," were discoverable by appellee because the term "civil action" referred to a tort action, not a disciplinary action before appellee. The court concluded that § 130A(a)(3) precluded discovery only by "persons", and appellee was not a person within the meaning of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the appellate court's judgment holding that the proceedings, records, and files of the hospital's medical review committee were discoverable. The court reversed the portion of the judgment finding that appellee Commission on Medical Discipline of Maryland could not subpoena the medical review committee's minutes and notes because only persons, not state agencies, were precluded from discovering such materials.

Wilson v. State


No. 120, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 664; 399 A.2d 256; 1979 Md. LEXIS 188



March 30, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Criminal Court of Baltimore, Baylor, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded to that court for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion; costs to be paid by the Mayor and City Council of Baltimore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) dismissed defendant's following his convictions for rape, robbery, and carnal knowledge of a victim. Defendant filed a petition for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted, he filed a petition seeking relief under post-conviction procedures. A lower court granted defendant a belated appeal on his allegations that the trial judge was prejudiced and that he was denied a speedy trial after it found that defendant's appellate counsel was ineffective. An appellate court dismissed defendant's appeal sua sponte. Defendant then filed for a writ of certiorari. The court held that under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 645A of the Maryland Post Conviction Procedure Act, defendant was entitled to obtain a belated appeal as a remedy because he was denied proper appellate review due to the improper action of his appellate counsel. The court found that the lower court had the power to grant a delayed appeal. Also, the appellate court had the power to review the appeal. Therefore, the court held that the appellate court erred when it dismissed defendant's appeal. The court concluded that defendant was entitled to appellate review of his claims of judicial prejudice and denial of a speedy trial. The judgment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision, which dismissed defendant's appeal, was reversed and remanded.

Langworthy v. State


No. 47, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 588; 399 A.2d 578; 1979 Md. LEXIS 183



March 28, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, McCullough, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; case remanded to that court for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion; costs to be paid by Prince George's County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) that dismissed his appeal from his conviction for rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape but the trial court found that he was insane at the time the crime was committed. Therefore, defendant was ordered committed to a state mental hospital. Defendant appealed from his conviction. The court of special appeals dismissed the appeal, and defendant sought review. The court reversed and remanded. A defendant was permitted to appeal from a final judgment entered in a criminal case. Despite the lack of a "sentence" in the context of punishment inflicted here, the determination of the trial court as to the disposition of defendant was as final a judgment following his conviction as if a sentence had been imposed. In the case of a finding of insanity, punishment was legislatively prohibited. Therefore, the general rule that pronouncement of sentence was required to comprise an appealable judgment did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing defendant's appeal from his conviction for rape was reversed and remanded.
