Cooper v. Wicomico County, Dep't of Public Works


No. 65, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 576; 398 A.2d 1237; 1979 Md. LEXIS 194



March 12, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County; Simpkins, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, asking to determine whether a supplemental worker's compensation award, which increased the amounts payable to the employee under a prior award for permanent total disability, unconstitutionally disturbed contractual or other vested rights of appellees, his employer and the employer's insurer.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained an accidental injury in his employment. The Commission found the employee was totally and permanently disabled and ordered that he be paid weekly compensation, not to exceed $ 30,000 in total, the maximum payable at that time under Md. Code art. 101, § 36(1)(a) (1957). The General Assembly added new Md. Code art. 101, § 36(10) directing how additional allowances were to be calculated. The result was to increase the weekly payments to the employee from $ 45.33 to $ 57.96 and the limit of the total payable to $ 38,397. The trial court found that the act could not constitutionally be applied retrospectively. The employee contended that the evidence was insufficient to show the extent, if any, of the injury actually caused appellees by the supplemental allowance payments. The court affirmed, finding that the operational effect of the act required insurers and hence employers to make payments for supplemental allowance benefits, which were not ultimately reimbursed, in amounts sufficient to constitute a substantial injury to constitutionally protected vested rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Massage Parlors, Inc. v. Baltimore


No. 19, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 490; 398 A.2d 52; 1979 Md. LEXIS 261



February 23, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court No. 2 of Baltimore City; Perrott, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree affirmed; appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court (Maryland), which was entered in favor of appellee city officials of Baltimore in a dispute concerning the revocation of the corporation's operator's permit.


OVERVIEW: The corporation's permit had been revoked because it was engaging in heterosexual massage. The corporation brought suit contending the ordinance regulating massage parlors was unconstitutional. The corporation argued that the ordinance was unconstitutional on its face because it promoted sex discrimination in violation of the equal protection clause of the fourteenth amendment of the United States Constitution and the Maryland Declaration of Rights. The court interpreted the ordinance as prohibiting simultaneous treatment of persons of both sexes in the same room; it did not establish any sexual distinction as to who could administer a massage to persons of either sex. The corporation argued the ordinance violated the equal protection clause of the fourteenth amendment in that it provided for invidious class legislation. The court determined the ordinance did not involve a fundamental right or suspect class. The court held there was no equal protection violation. The corporation also challenged the means by which the city sought to achieve a legitimate governmental objective. The court held the means utilized were reasonable and rational.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which was entered in favor of the city officials of Baltimore in the action involving the revocation of the corporation's permit.

Comprehensive Accounting Service Co. v. Maryland State Board of Public Accountancy


No. 51, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 474; 397 A.2d 1019; 1979 Md. LEXIS 231; 4 A.L.R.4th 1188



February 22, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Baltimore City; Sullivan and Perrott, JJ., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decree reversed; costs to be paid by appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accounting firm sought review of an adverse decision by the Circuit Court of Baltimore (Maryland) in an action by appellee Maryland State Board of Public Accountancy to enjoin the firm from violating the provisions of Md. Ann. Code art. 75A, § 14(e) by holding itself out to the public as performing accounting services when it did not hold an enrollment certificate to practice public accounting in Maryland.


OVERVIEW: The board brought an action under Md. Ann. Code art. 75A, § 14(e) to enjoin the non-certified accounting firm from holding itself out to the public as providing accounting services. The court reversed a judgment for the board and found that § 14(e)'s prohibition on the firm's use of the words "accountant" and "accounting" in describing its services to the public was inconsistent with commercial free speech principles and, therefore, violated U.S. Const. amend. I. Md. Ann. Code art. 75A, § 15(e) expressly authorized the firm to perform accounting services for the public, while at the same time Md. Ann. Code art. 75A, § 14(e) prohibited it from describing those services to the public as accounting, or holding itself out to the public as an accountant. The court ruled that the legislature could not choose the most drastic remedy of completely suppressing the use of certain words to describe the firm's lawful activity as a non-certified accountant. Because the board failed to show that there was a compelling need for the restraint on the firm's commercial speech, the court dissolved the injunction and held that Md. Ann. Code art. 75A, § 14(e) violated the firm's free speech rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment for the board in its action to enjoin the firm from holding itself out to the public as an accounting firm and as offering accounting services even though it was not certified to practice accounting in the state.

Annapolis v. Annapolis Waterfront Co.


No. 6, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 383; 396 A.2d 1080; 1979 Md. LEXIS 165



January 24, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed February 13, 1979; Denied February 16, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Williams, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed; remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the decree of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County and to remand to that court with instructions to enter a decree consistent with the views expressed herein. Costs to be paid by appellees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the mayor, the aldermen, and others (the city), sought review of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the trial court's decision reversing the city's denial of permits necessary for appellees, a condominium developer and a council of unit owners, to construct additional boat slips for use by the condominium owners. The trial court ordered the city to grant the necessary permits.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought approval from the port wardens to build additional boat slips for its condominiums, and the request was denied based upon adverse environmental and traffic effects. Pursuant to Annapolis, Md., City Charter § 40 (1970), the developer sought de novo review from the mayor and aldermen, who also denied the permit. The trial court reversed the city's denial and entered a mandatory injunction ordering the city to grant the permit. The appellate court affirmed, and the court reversed, holding that there was substantial evidence in the record for the city's determination. The court found that: (1) there was no conflict between § 38 of the Charter, which set forth the powers of the port wardens, and Md. Ann. Code art. 23A, § 2(23A) (1974), because the purpose of both was to allow the wardens to regulate construction on the waterways; (2) thus, it was error for the trial court to find that the city was unable to consider environmental factors, where it was not prohibited by § 2(23A); and (3) the trial court improperly substituted its judgment where there was substantial evidence to support the city's denial of permits and where the issue was fairly debatable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment affirming the trial court's reversal of the city's decision to deny necessary permits for the developer to construct additional boat slips. The court remanded to the appellate court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand to the trial court with instructions for it to enter a decree in favor of the city.

Pope v. State


No. 11, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 309; 396 A.2d 1054; 1979 Md. LEXIS 174; 1 A.L.R.4th 1



January 19, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Fairbanks, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals with respect to child abuse, third count of Indictment No. 18666, reversing the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, affirmed; judgments of the Court of Special Appeals with respect to misprision of felony, fifth count of Indictment No. 18666, affirming the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County, reversed; case remanded to Court of Special Appeals with direction to remand to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County for entry of judgment of acquittal on the third count and dismissal of the fifth count; motion of appellant to strike granted; motion of appellant for appropriate relief denied; costs to be paid by Montgomery County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a nine-count indictment with offenses related to the death of a child. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), entered judgment convicting defendant of child abuse in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35A and misprision of felony under common law. On review, the Court of Special Appeals affirmed the misprision conviction, but reversed the conviction for abuse. The State and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A three-month-old infant died as a result of physical injuries inflicted by his mother. The abuse by the mother occurred while the mother and infant were staying in defendant's home. Defendant was present in the home during the incident. Defendant was subsequently charged in a nine-count indictment. Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of child abuse in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35A and misprision of felony under common law. Defendant sought review, and the court of special appeals reversed the child abuse conviction and affirmed the misprision of felony conviction. Defendant and the State then petitioned for certiorari with the court. The court found evidentiary insufficiency with respect to the conviction for child abuse, both as a principal in the first degree and as a principal in the second degree, so that the judgment of the trial court on the evidence was clearly erroneous. As to the conviction for misprision of felony, the court held misprision of felony was not a chargeable offense, and, thus, dismissal of that charge was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed with respect to reversal of the conviction for child abuse. The judgment was reversed with respect to the conviction for misprision of felony. The matter was remanded with direction for entry of judgment of acquittal on the child abuse count and dismissal of the misprision of felony count.

Clark v. State


Nos. 72, 74, 75, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 260; 396 A.2d 243; 1979 Md. LEXIS 172



January 5, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (No. 72) Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County; Hopper, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.

(Nos. 74 and 75) Two appeals from the Circuit Court for Queen Anne's County; Turner, J, pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in each of Clark v. State, No. 72, September Term, 1978; Stutzman v. State, No. 74, September Term, 1978; and Pritchard v. State, No. 75, September Term, 1978, affirmed. Costs to be paid by each appellant in the amount chargeable to him.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants escaped from a place in the state in which they had been legally confined and they were thereafter duly charged, convicted, and sentenced by the Court of Anne Arundel County (Maryland) pursuant to the provisions of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 139(a) (1957). Defendants sought review and certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the three-year exception of § 139(a) for juvenile offenders violated the guarantees of equal protection. The court assumed that defendants had standing, rejected this claim and the other sentencing claims, and affirmed the lower court's judgments. The court held that equal protection prohibited arbitrary classifications and required that classifications have a reasonable basis. The court found that the three-year exception in the punishment of juvenile offenders for escape was sufficiently related to a legitimate state interest in confining juveniles where they would not intermingle with older, seasoned, and dangerous criminals. Thus, the court upheld the classification as constitutionally valid. The court also rejected the claim of one defendant that he was improperly sentenced. The court held that the lower court's remarks that this defendant might be able to find and retain a job if his hair was cut did not evidence prejudice, ill will, or that the sentence was based upon impermissible considerations. The court also held that another defendant was properly before the lower court because he voluntarily submitted to its jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgments.

 

393 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ward


No. 66, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 189; 396 A.2d 1041; 1978 Md. LEXIS 465



December 21, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals in one record from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Blackwell, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; case remanded for trial in accordance with this opinion; motion to dismiss cross-appeal granted; costs to be paid by appellee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of an order in favor of defendant from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which dismissed the indictment against defendant as an accessory before the fact in a murder after the principals pled guilty to second-degree murder. Defendant filed a cross-appeal for dismissal based on double jeopardy and the prosecution filed a motion to dismiss the cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with as an accessory before the fact in a murder alleged to have been committed by two other individuals. The principals plead guilty to second-degree murder. The trial court dismissed the indictment against defendant as defective. The prosecution maintained that defendant could be found guilty of murder as an accessory before the fact even when the principals were only convicted of second degree murder. The prosecution sought review and defendant filed a cross-appeal based on double jeopardy to which the prosecution filed a motion to dismiss. On appeal the court reversed and remanded for a new trial and held that: (1) defendant could be convicted of accessory before the fact of murder in the second-degree; (2) defendant as an accessory could not be convicted of a higher crime than the principals and therefore, defendant could not be convicted of first-degree murder; and (3) defendant's cross-appeal based on double jeopardy was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the indictment against defendant and granted the prosecution's motion to dismiss defendant's cross-appeal.

 

394 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Curtis v. State


No. 153, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 132; 395 A.2d 464; 1978 Md. LEXIS 451



December 18, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed January 16, 1979; Denied January 31, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Couch and Woods, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed and case remanded to the Court of Special Appeals for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Costs to be paid by Prince George's County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), to challenge its decision to dismiss his petition for postconviction relief, which had alleged the inadequacy of his counsel at trial, on appeal, and in his first petition for postconviction relief, under the Maryland Postconviction Procedure Act, Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 645A.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner raised for the first time, in his second petition for postconviction relief, that he had been deprived of his Sixth Amendment right to the genuine and effective representation of counsel. The trial court granted the state's motion to dismiss the petition because it ruled that he had waived these allegations for purposes of review by failing to raise the issues previously. The intermediate appellate court agreed. After granting a writ of certiorari, the court ruled that the presumption of waiver did not apply absent a showing that the waiver was intelligent and knowing. The intelligent and knowing standard did not apply if the waiver was part of counsel's trial tactics. Petitioner could not be precluded from having his issue of inadequate assistance of counsel being considered because of his mere failure to raise the issue previously. The proffered facts disclosed that petitioner did not intelligently and knowingly fail to previously raise the matter of his trial counsel's alleged inadequacy and the issue could not be deemed to have been waived.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case because the lower court had not reached the issue of the inadequacy of representation by petitioner's trial counsel.

 

395 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Dorsey v. English


No. 165, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


283 Md. 522; 390 A.2d 1133; 1978 Md. LEXIS 428



September 14, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Woods, Robert J., J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed a petition to establish paternity of her son in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland). During the course of the trial the child was exhibited to the jury and the mother was permitted to point out resemblances between the child and defendant putative father. The jury returned a verdict that defendant was the father and from the judgment entered thereon, he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The putative father made a number of contentions, but his primary complaint was that the trial court permitted the child to be exhibited to the jury. The trial court examined a child two years and five months old and compared his features with the putative father. He then permitted the child to be exhibited to the jury. The court found no abuse of the trial court's discretion. The putative father also posed the secondary issue of whether the mother should have been allowed to point out to the jury the particular physical features of the child which she believed to be similar to the putative father's. The jury had ample opportunity to make a comparison and to weigh the probative force and reliability of the testimony of the witnesses. Thus, the trial court properly admitted the mother's testimony. The putative father next attacked Maryland's paternity statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 16, § 66 A-O (1957), as unconstitutional. The court found there was a rational relation between the purpose of that statute and the means utilized to achieve it by placing the responsibility for a child's welfare and support on the parents. Thus, the statute held him and her equally responsible for support.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

396 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. 155, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


283 Md. 358; 390 A.2d 1112; 1978 Md. LEXIS 425



August 18, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Dorchester County; Edmondson, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appellant to pay costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review on a writ of certiorari of his conviction in the Circuit Court for Dorchester County (Maryland) for possessing illegal crabs in violation of Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 4-809 (1974). The conviction under review was imposed following his trial de novo after his similar conviction in a district court. He contended that Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. §§ 4-809(a), 4-102(a) (1974) violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possessing undersized crabs among a truckload of crabs that he was transporting from Virginia to a Maryland processing plant. The court affirmed his conviction and found that Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. §§ 4-809(a), 4-102(a) (1974) did not constitute unlawful protectionism and that the statutes furthered legitimate local public interest. Moreover, the court ruled that, on balance, the statutes did not so unduly burden interstate commerce as to render them unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, and that they were constitutional. The court held that the applicable legislative scheme effected conservation of the state's natural resources, which was a legitimate local public interest, and that the laws concerning crabs were a material aspect of that scheme. It was not material that the crabs had been harvested in another state and had been shipped to him from that state in an original package in which he had received and exposed them for sale. The court also found that Md. Code Ann., Nat. Res. § 4-809(a) (1974) was not unconstitutionally vague, either on its face or as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of illegal crabs.

 

397 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Board of Supervisors of Elections v. Goodsell


No. 36, September Term, 1978


Court of Appeals of Maryland


284 Md. 279; 396 A.2d 1033; 1978 Md. LEXIS 466



July 28, 1978  
January 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County; Blackwell, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Board of Supervisors of Elections of Prince George's County, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which issued a writ of mandamus directing the Board to accept appellee candidate's certificate of candidacy for the office of County Executive and to place his name on a ballot after the Board refused to do so in reliance on Prince George's County, Maryland Charter art. IV, § 405.


OVERVIEW: Section 405 required the County Executive to have been a "qualified voter" for at least five years preceding his election. The candidate had been a resident of the county for more than five years, but had only been a registered voter for two years. He filed a certificate of candidacy, which the Board refused to accept because the candidate had not been a registered voter for five years. On appeal, the Board asserted that the term "qualified voter" in § 405 meant that the candidate had to have been registered. The candidate asserted that the term meant simply that he had to have been qualified to vote, which he was, and not actually registered. He also asserted that the requirement violated Equal Protection. The court disagreed with the trial court's interpretation that the term "qualified voter" did not require registration. Other provisions of the county's charter which used the term demonstrated the intent that a "qualified voter" was one who was registered. However, the provision violated Equal Protection. In applying strict scrutiny, based upon the affect the provision had on voters, the court found that the Board failed to show a "compelling governmental interest."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment issuing the writ of mandamus.

 

398 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Lebedun v. State


No. 154, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


283 Md. 257; 390 A.2d 64; 1978 Md. LEXIS 420



July 18, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County, Fairbanks, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Special Appeals reversed and case remanded to that court with instructions to reverse the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County and to remand for a new trial; costs to be paid by Montgomery County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the defendant's conviction for two armed robberies and handgun violations. The trial court had consolidated the offenses at trial and denied defendant's motion to suppress seized evidence and a statement subsequent to his arrest.


OVERVIEW: The police entered defendant's hotel room with a rescue squad, after defendant called for an ambulance, and arrested defendant. Defendant was charged with two drug store robberies. The trial court consolidated the trial on the two charges over defendant's objection. Defendant was convicted of the robberies and appealed the trial court denial of his motion to suppress the evidence seized from the hotel room and subsequent statement, and the denial of his motion opposing the consolidation of the two robbery counts. The appeals court affirmed the defendant's conviction. The court reversed the decision of the appeals court and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held that the entry of the police officer into the hotel room was an emergency circumstance which required no warrant because the officer was there for the purpose of protecting the rescue squad and a delay to obtain a search warrant would have permitted destruction of the evidence. The court found that the defendant was prejudiced by consolidating the two robberies for trial. The evidence of the defendant's guilt on either of the charges would not have admissible at separate trials.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appeals court, with instructions to reverse the judgement of the trial court and remand the case.

 

399 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Robert T. Foley Co. v. Washington Suburban Sanitary Com.


No. 90, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


283 Md. 140; 389 A.2d 350; 1978 Md. LEXIS 413



July 14, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County; Frosh, J., pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated. Case remanded to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County for the entry of a judgment in conformance with this opinion. Costs to be paid by the appellants-respondents, Robert T. Foley Company et al. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which granted the motion for summary judgment of respondent sanitary commission in the developers' action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief concerning the validity of sewer service charges levied upon the developers by the sanitary commission.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the moratoria on new sewer authorizations were necessary to prevent the increasing discharge of raw and inadequately treated sewage into the waters of the state. The court held that in light of the comprehensive character of the problem faced by the sanitary commission, the program proposed for resolution of the problem and financed by a uniformly levied charge was reasonable. The court held that the charge was not unconstitutional on substantive due process grounds. The court held that the resolution represented a valid exercise of the police power and, under the specific circumstances of this case, did not impair any contract rights of the developers with regard to the increase in charges. However, the court held that the circuit court erred by failing to set forth in its judgment a declaration of the parties' rights with regard to the issues raised and, therefore, vacated the judgment and remanded the case to the circuit court for a new judgment that included a declaration of the parties' rights.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the circuit court's judgment in favor of the sanitary commission in the developers' action seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, remanded to the circuit court, and ordered the developers to pay costs.

 

400 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Bowers v. State


No. 150, September Term, 1977


Court of Appeals of Maryland


283 Md. 115; 389 A.2d 341; 1978 Md. LEXIS 411



July 13, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County, Evans, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; costs to be paid by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) for committing child abuse against his stepdaughter in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35A (1973). On appeal, he asserted that the statute was so vague and indefinite that it violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the federal Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35A (1973) prohibited child abuse, which it defined as any physical injury sustained by a child as a result of "cruel or inhumane" treatment or as a result of "malicious acts" by a parent "or any other person who has permanent or temporary care or custody" of the child. Defendant was convicted of violating § 35A by beating his stepdaughter on her back, neck, arm, and legs with a belt for skipping school. Defendant attacked § 35A by asserting that the terms "cruel or inhumane" and "temporary care or custody" were so vague and indefinite that the statute violated the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held that in applying a strict specificity standard and in determining whether the statute gave a fair warning of the prohibited conduct and adequate guidelines for law enforcement, the statute was sufficiently definite to withstand constitutional attack. The terms "cruel or inhumane" and "malicious" had acquired a relatively widely accepted connotation in the common law, and the use of such phraseology in the child abuse statute did not render it constitutionally infirm. The terms "temporary care or custody" were also sufficiently definite.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.
